Central Propaganda Department Receives the Press

The Central Propaganda Department held a press conference at 2:00 PM on the 27th in the Central Second Conference Hall. More than 20 reporters from various newspapers attended. Liu Luyin chaired the meeting and reported to the reporters, stating that since Yan Xishan sent out the Zeng Xiao telegrams, their content has been deeply known to the people of the country. Today, the Central Government has received the Yang telegram from Yan, the content of which is even more bizarre than the previous telegrams. Although the telegrams repeatedly sent by Yan appear peaceful on the surface, they are actually preparing to use force, nominally seeking the unity of the entire party, but in reality, they are a grand alliance of warlords, bureaucrats, imperialist running dogs, and local bandit leaders. As for the generals who signed the Yang telegram, many of them were using false names, and some had no connection with Yan or had long been relieved of their military power. In addition, there were many bandit leaders who were also signed in. The content of the telegram advocated a national consensus to decide on national policies. Yan's intention was nothing more than to unite the Anfu clique, the Research clique, Zhang Zongchang, Wu Peifu, Duan Qirui, and others into one force. Yan has also claimed that Shanxi's autonomy has been quite successful and that he is the only one who can resolve national policies. In fact, according to the latest investigations, Yan's policy of governing Shanxi is to find ways to make all useful talents leave Shanxi or make them addicted to opium. The so-called village chiefs, district chiefs, and township chiefs are all addicted to opium. It is rumored that Yan will organize a temporary government in Beiping, with Feng in charge of military affairs and Yan in charge of internal affairs. If this rumor is true, it will at most lead to a situation where opium addiction is rampant throughout Shanxi. Also, Shanxi's annual income is about 20 million, while consumer spending requires 60 million, resulting in a financial deficit. Therefore, Yan has taken all the cash from several provinces, including Hebei, and circulated Shanxi paper money in provinces such as Hebei. Yan also said that the South has boundaries with the North, but in fact, Yan only uses people from Shanxi, which is purely feudal thinking. Now Yan has entered a dead end and wants to deceive the people of the country in the name of concession. In fact, even the people of Shanxi and Hebei will not be deceived by this kind of rhetoric. Now, the only way to deal with Yan is to ask the people of the country to give Yan a final general judgment with justice and revolutionary theory, without having to reason with him. As for the people in the North, they have expressed their resistance to Yan's actions. Although Yan does not dare to openly close down mass organizations and institutions, the inspection of telegrams and the conscription of military grain have caused unease in Northern society. The meeting was adjourned after the report.

The National Government Stipulates Methods for Appealing Against Illegal Acts of Administrative Officials

The Executive Yuan is the Highest Decision-Making Body

The National Government yesterday issued a special order to all directly subordinate agencies, informing them that the Executive Yuan should be the highest decision-making body for appeals against illegal acts of administrative agencies. The order stated: "It is hereby ordered that the previous approval of the Central Political Council's reply regarding the issue of which agency to file administrative lawsuits against illegal acts of administrative agencies was handed over to Committee Member Wang Chonghui for research. According to the reply, before the establishment of the Administrative Court, one may temporarily invoke the old Law on Appeals to file appeals. Please investigate and comply with the above. As for the central and local highest administrative agencies of the old Law on Appeals, which should be determined first, two proposed methods were submitted for approval by the Civil Service Office of the National Government: (1) The final decision on inappropriate dispositions under the old Law on Appeals shall be made by the Executive Yuan; (2) According to the old Law on Appeals, those who have declared dissatisfaction within the statutory period may still file a re-appeal with the superior administrative agency. The above methods have been submitted to the 64th State Council Meeting of the National Government for approval. In addition to distributing them separately, you are hereby ordered to acknowledge and instruct your subordinates to comply accordingly."

Ecuador Will Ban Imports

The Ministry of Health Determined that it is a Narcotic Drug

Handled in Accordance with Item D of Article 14 of the Hague Convention

The Central Anti-Opium Committee previously received a letter from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, stating that the International League of Nations had stated in a letter that the Geneva Anti-Opium Convention's proposed recommendations considered five kinds of drugs, including Ecuador, as narcotic drugs, which have the same harmful effects as the drugs to which the convention applies. It was asked whether China intended to apply the provisions of Item D of Article 14 of the Hague Anti-Opium Convention to the above-mentioned drugs. The committee immediately submitted a request to the Executive Yuan for instructions on whether the five kinds of drugs should be subject to the provisions of Item D of Article 14 of the Hague Anti-Opium Convention, so as to prevent their import and eliminate abuses. Subsequently, the Executive Yuan transferred the matter to the Ministry of Health for verification. According to the reply, the five kinds of drugs, including Ecuador, are derivatives or preparations of opium components, which can all be used as substitutes for opium. If they are continued to be taken, they have the same harmful effects and impacts as opium and should naturally also be regarded as narcotic drugs. The provisions of Item D of Article 14 of the Hague Anti-Opium Convention should be applied to prohibit their import. It is heard that the Executive Yuan has transferred the order to the Anti-Opium Committee for investigation and handling.

Jiangsu Province Measures for Banning Silkworm Seed Industry

The Jiangsu Provincial Government decided on the following provisional measures for banning the silkworm seed industry at the 267th meeting on the 25th: (Article 1) Any silkworm seed manufacturers within the territory of Jiangsu Province, regardless of public or private operation, shall be banned in accordance with these measures. The term "silkworm seed manufacturer" in these measures refers to those who manufacture silkworm seeds for the purpose of supplying them to others, but this does not apply to those who supply them for academic research. (Article 2) Silkworm seed manufacturers must be registered with the Department of Agriculture and Mines and issued a license. (Article 3) Silkworm seed manufacturers must have equipment to prevent the occurrence of the following silkworm diseases: 1. Pebrine disease, 2. Flacherie, 3. Grasserie, 4. Muscardine, 5. Silkworm maggots (Article 4) Silkworm seed manufacturers may not manufacture silkworm seeds without using original silkworm seeds. (Article 5) Silkworm seed manufacturers may not engage in silkworm cocoon breeding and may not raise original silkworms in ordinary silkworm rearing rooms. (Article 6) When manufacturing original silkworm seeds, one egg shall be used for one moth, but when necessary, it may be changed with the permission of the Silkworm Industry Control Office of the Department of Agriculture and Mines. (Article 7) Original silkworm seeds shall be manufactured using bags or frames, and ordinary silkworm seeds shall be manufactured using frames. (Article 8) Original silkworm seeds shall be subject to inspection of silkworm eggs, silkworm larvae, silkworm cocoons, and parent moths, but with the approval of the Department of Agriculture and Mines through the Silkworm Industry Control Office of the Department of Agriculture and Mines, they may temporarily conduct self-inspection, and personnel will be dispatched by the Silkworm Industry Control Office of the Department of Agriculture and Mines to conduct random re-inspection on-site. (Article 9) Ordinary silkworm seeds shall be subject to inspection of silkworm larvae, silkworm cocoons, and parent moths, but the parent moth inspection shall be temporarily conducted by the silkworm seed manufacturer, and personnel will be dispatched by the Silkworm Industry Control Office of the Department of Agriculture and Mines at any time to conduct random re-inspection on-site. (Article 10) In accordance with the provisions of Articles 8 and 9, qualified silkworm seeds shall have a certificate of qualification affixed to the paper or container, and unqualified silkworm seeds shall be burned. (Article 11) Silkworm seeds without a certificate of qualification shall not be sold or transferred. (Article 12) Silkworm seeds imported from other provinces or foreign countries must have a certificate of qualification from the place of origin, unless specially approved by the Department of Agriculture and Mines. When necessary, the Silkworm Industry Control Office of the Department of Agriculture and Mines may still conduct a re-inspection. (Article 13) Methods of selling that hinder the physiology of silkworm seeds shall be prohibited. (Article 14) The varieties of original silkworm seeds may be designated by the Department of Agriculture and Mines when it deems necessary. (Article 15) Silkworm seed manufacturers may organize a Silkworm Seed Industry Association with the approval of the Department of Agriculture and Mines, and its regulations shall be formulated separately. (Article 16) The Silkworm Industry Control Office of the Department of Agriculture and Mines may send personnel to each silkworm seed manufacturing plant at any time to conduct inspections and inquiries, and may request inspection items when necessary. (Article 17) Personnel from the Silkworm Industry Control Office of the Department of Agriculture and Mines shall avoid inspecting silkworm seed manufacturing plants in which they have invested or operate themselves. (Article 18) Personnel from the Silkworm Industry Control Office of the Department of Agriculture and Mines may not concurrently serve as staff members of silkworm seed manufacturing plants. (Article 19) If the actions of a silkworm seed manufacturer violate these measures or violate orders issued based on these measures, the Department of Agriculture and Mines may suspend or restrict its business or even cancel it. (Article 20) Those who violate the provisions of Articles 4 shall be fined up to 60 yuan. (Article 21) Those who manufacture silkworm seeds for the purpose of supplying them to others without being registered with the Department of Agriculture and Mines and issued a license shall be fined up to 80 yuan in addition to confiscating the manufactured silkworm seeds. (Article 22) Those who use fraudulent acts to respond to the inspection of Articles 8 and 9 shall be fined up to 100 yuan. (Article 23) Inspection personnel who engage in favoritism and corruption or extort money under false pretenses shall be severely punished according to law. (Article 24) The amount of the fine and the name of the fined person shall be announced in the Agriculture and Mines Gazette. (Article 25) The detailed rules for the implementation of these measures shall be formulated separately by the Department of Agriculture and Mines and reported to the Provincial Government for record. (Article 26) If there are any matters not covered in these measures, the Department of Agriculture and Mines may request the Provincial Government to amend them. (Article 27) These measures shall be implemented from the date of promulgation.

Continued Records of the Anhui Northern Rehabilitation Conference

Bengbu Correspondence: The Anhui Northern Counties Rehabilitation Conference held its third meeting at Tang Garden on the morning of the 23rd, starting at 9:00 AM. Thirty-five people attended, chaired by Yuan Lizhen. The following resolutions were passed: (1) Regarding the eleven articles of the "Temporary Measures for Handling Local Militias in 21 Counties of Northern Anhui" (hereinafter referred to as the "Temporary Measures"), and how they should be followed: (1) It was resolved that Articles 1, 2, 3, 7, 10, and 11 of the Temporary Measures did not require discussion. (2) Regarding Article 5 of the Temporary Measures, it was resolved to add the following supplementary opinion: "If the existing 7,965 rifles, pistols, mortars, and machine guns of the local militias in each county are insufficient, they may be borrowed from the public." (3) Regarding Article 6 of the Temporary Measures, it was resolved to appoint Jiang Shuxun, Peng Zhenqiu, Ge Kunshan, Song Shike, and Liu Yihua as drafting committee members to participate in the army's organizational structure and incorporate local conditions to draft organizational methods, to be convened by Song Shike. (4) Regarding Article 8 of the Temporary Measures, it was resolved to add the following supplementary opinion: "The expenses of the self-defense corps in each county shall be managed by the county magistrate, who shall oversee the local financial management office. If there are any cases of embezzlement or misappropriation, the county magistrate shall handle them according to the law at any time." Ge Kunshan and Song Shike moved to request the cancellation of the district corps system in Article 9 of the Temporary Measures, which was resolved to pass. (5) Regarding the resolution on Article 9 of the Temporary Measures, the office shall submit a request to the provincial government to abolish the district corps leader system based on the resolutions of the rehabilitation conference. (2) Regarding the suppression of bandits, it was resolved to incorporate it into the case of suppressing bandits in the counties of Northern Anhui. The meeting adjourned at 12:00 PM.

The fourth meeting was held at 2:00 PM, with 37 attendees, chaired by Yuan Lizhen. The following resolutions were passed: (1) Regarding the relief of disaster victims in Northern Anhui (proposed by the first group of the office), it was resolved: (1) That the office organize a temporary emergency relief committee for Northern Anhui, to be established promptly, to handle emergency relief matters. (2) That the National Government Disaster Relief Committee be requested, and telegrams be sent to various Shanghai charitable organizations and native-place associations in various provinces, to raise relief funds. (3) That the county governments and public organizations in each county be ordered to assist in the handling of relief efforts. Song Shike and Ge Kunshan moved to request compensation for losses during last year's winter incident, which was resolved that if there were receipts for funds forcibly taken from each county during the incident, they should be compiled and submitted to the office for verification and submission for approval. Wu Zhenwu moved to request compensation for local supplies and losses forcibly taken during last year's winter incident, which was resolved that the county governments and chambers of commerce of each county should ascertain the exact amounts and submit them to the office for verification and submission for relief. (2) Regarding the collection of overdue land taxes (proposed by the second group of the office), it was resolved to pass the original proposal. (3) Regarding the investigation of various public funds at the county level (proposed by the second group of the office), it was resolved that the county magistrates should ascertain the details, truthfully compile registers, and report them to the public in the entire county. If there were any cases of embezzlement, they should be reported and handled according to the law. The meeting adjourned at 5:00 PM.

Garrison Troops in Western Hunan Encircle and Suppress Zhou Chaowu

Now Pressing Towards Dayong County

Changsha Correspondence on the 20th: He Long and Zhou Chaowu are both well-known bandit leaders in Western Hunan, who have ravaged the local area and committed heinous crimes. Last year, He Long seized Sangzhi, raised the red banner high, and massacred civilians. After being severely suppressed by the military corps, he led his bandit troops to flee to Hefeng in western Hubei. However, Zhou Chaowu still occupies Dayong, secretly colluding with He Long. The Hunan Anti-Banditry Command believes that if He and Zhou are not eliminated quickly, the people of Western Hunan will never have peace of mind. In addition to consulting with the military authorities of the three provinces of Hubei, Sichuan, and Hunan to jointly suppress He Long, the task of suppressing Zhou Chaowu has been entrusted to Dai Douyuan, the Anti-Banditry Commander of Western Hunan, who has personally gone to supervise the suppression. After receiving the order, Dai set off from Changde to Cili on the 9th of this month to supervise the military corps in a large-scale encirclement and suppression. According to reports, on the 16th, the bandit troops were heavily defeated in Yankou, Tankou, and Laoyakou in Dayong, with many killed and captured. The troops are now pressing towards Dayong County, pursuing and attacking, and have sent a telegram to the province reporting the situation. The telegram states: A. Zhou Chaowu sent his bandit party Zhou Dushu to lead 600-700 bandit troops to occupy Yankou; Zhang Yi led 700-800 bandit troops to occupy Tankou; Li Dewu led 600-700 bandit troops to occupy Laoyakou; and Li Ziyuan led 300-400 bandit troops to occupy Zhengjiaping, totaling over 2,000 people, blocking our troops along the way. B. I ordered the Tian Regiment to lead the Xing Independent Battalion to attack the bandit troops in Laoyakou from Jinyanshan; the Liu Regiment to attack the bandit troops in Tankou from Tankouping; and the main force, together with the Cili militia led by Wang Yuqi, to attack the bandit troops in Yankou from Jiashikou; and Xu Chuanshu to supervise the militia to attack the bandit troops in Zhengjiaping from Baizhangxia. All were ordered to act simultaneously at dawn today (the 16th) to clear out the bandit troops and press towards Dayong. C. According to reports from the Tian and Liu Regiments, who contacted us by telephone from Xikou, the attack situation is summarized as follows: (1) The Tian Regiment came into contact with the enemy troops in Laoyakou at 6:00 AM today. After about three hours of fierce fighting, the bandits launched a fierce assault on our troops. After our artillery and machine guns fired with full force, our officers and soldiers advanced bravely and launched a flanking attack on the right wing, and the bandits were defeated. The bandits in Tankou fled to Chenjiashan. By noon today, our troops had successively occupied the three passes and are now pressing towards Dayong City to pursue and attack. (2) A total of over 50 bandits were killed, over 100 were wounded, over 40 miscellaneous rifles, 3 pistols, and 1 submachine gun were seized. 15 of our soldiers were wounded and 4 were killed. (3) The Xu Chuanshu troops who went out of Baizhangxia did not report because they were on a flanking mission and were far from my position. D. In addition to ordering the front-line troops to continue to pursue and attack with all their might to eliminate the bandits, the situation of the attack on the three passes today is hereby reported for your review.

Missing Airplane Found in Liling

Two Pilots Found Dead Inside

Changsha Correspondence: The First Air Squadron of the Aviation Department, which was transferred to Guangdong last December to participate in the campaign against Zhang Gui, returned to Wuhan from Guangdong after the Tang Department's rebellion. On December 20th, three planes took off from Guangdong. One plane braved the weather and arrived in Wuhan, one returned to Guangzhou, and one went missing in Hunan. Repeated telegrams were sent to the counties of southern Hunan to search for it, but to no avail. The Aviation Department offered a reward of 1,000 yuan to encourage people to report information. After more than a month, there was still no news. Unexpectedly, on the 24th of this month, the Fourth Route Headquarters suddenly received a report from Hong Hangxian, a code clerk of the 15th Division, stating that his home was in Youwu, Liling West First District. Yesterday, on his way back to the unit from home, he met his cousin Hong Caigui, who told him that Luo Yongnian, who lived in Huang Gou Lian Chao, a small place in Luojia Ridge, had seen a plane fall on the mountain while cutting firewood on the 22nd of this month. There were two dead people inside, as well as two Browning pistols. At the same time, Liling County also telegraphed that a crashed plane had been found in Yaochang Temple, Liling West Third District, with two decomposed bodies inside and two Browning pistols. Personnel have been dispatched to investigate, and further details will be reported later. After receiving the report, the Headquarters dispatched Kuang Shengtao, a member of the Transportation Department, to investigate, and also sent a letter to Zhou Xicheng, the head of the Changsha Machine Department, asking him to send Zhang Shitong, a staff member, to go to Luojia Ridge, Liling, with the informant Hong Hangxian to investigate. Kuang, Zhang, and Hong took the early train to Zhuping on the 25th. (25th)

Financial Reorganization Measures in Guangdong Province

From the 19th, all Taxes in the Province Will Be Collected in Silver Dollars

The Central Bank Will Have a Capital of 80 Million in One Year

Tax Increase Allocated to Central Bank Permanent Fund

Additional Exchange Branches Opened to Exchange Various Paper Currencies

Guangzhou Correspondence: Recently, due to the war in Guangxi Province and the heavy military expenditures, the Central Bank's banknotes have been slightly affected. The unredeemed five-yuan, ten-yuan, fifty-yuan, and one-hundred-yuan notes are worth about 76-77% of their face value on the market. The redeemed one-yuan notes, because the Central Bank has recently been redeeming them with old silver dollars, and the market discriminates against old dollars, have also been affected, and now only worth 92% of their face value in new silver dollars. Seeing this situation, the authorities took this opportunity to thoroughly reorganize the Central Bank's capital, seeking a permanent and solid foundation. Huang Jusu, the newly appointed member of the Provincial Government, proposed this at the Provincial Affairs Conference, which was approved and announced by the Finance Department for implementation. The fundamental method is to collect all taxes in the province in cash, and all government expenditures will be paid in banknotes. The cash received will be used to purchase banknotes from the Central Bank, which will increase the Central Bank's capital day by day, and the Central Bank will be able to resume unlimited redemption. As for supplementing the Central Bank's current capital, it is planned to borrow from Guangzhou's rentals for one month within this month, which will yield about one million yuan, and to collect grain taxes in advance, which will yield about

Page 10

four million yuan, totaling five million yuan. Adding the revenue from the provincial treasury and the national treasury, more than ten million yuan can be obtained in the short term, and 80 million yuan can be obtained in one year. The Central Bank's capital has been permanently consolidated. In order to realize unlimited redemption, the Central Bank can set up five to ten additional exchange branches in the market within one month to facilitate the public's redemption of notes. After March 10th, new silver dollars can be redeemed. The government is willing to recoin the old coins, even if it loses 30,000 yuan for every million yuan. If the Central Bank's capital is sufficient, the five-yuan and one-hundred-yuan notes can also be restored to redemption in a few months. The financial reorganization measures announced by the Finance Department are listed below: (1) All taxes and levies collected by the Finance Department and the Special Envoy's Office are completely collected in silver dollars, and all cash will be allocated to the Central Bank's reserve fund and absolutely cannot be used for other purposes. In order to increase the reserve fund and fully restore redemption as soon as possible, all taxes and levies will still be collected with an additional 10% surcharge. (2) In addition to the above-mentioned tax revenues supplementing the Central Bank as a reserve fund, the Finance Department will formulate measures within three days to raise 5 million yuan in cash and transfer it to the Central Bank as a reserve fund. These measures will be submitted for decision and implementation at the next meeting. (3) In order to facilitate the people, the Central Bank should establish five to ten additional redemption offices in Guangzhou this month to facilitate the redemption of banknotes that have been announced to be restored to redemption. (4) In order to increase the public's confidence in Central Bank's notes, the Central Bank should hand over all the current old dollars and the old dollars gradually allocated from the Finance Department and the Special Envoy's Office to the Mint to be recoined into new dollars, and stipulate that from March 1st, both new and old dollars will be used for redemption in equal parts, and from March 10th, all new dollars will be used for redemption. (5) The Finance Department should assess the situation and announce the restoration of redemption of the five-yuan, ten-yuan, fifty-yuan, and one-hundred-yuan banknotes in the shortest possible time, separately and successively. (6) All expenditures of the Party, government, and military agencies of the Finance Department and the Special Envoy's Office will be paid in banknotes that have been restored to redemption. (7) The Finance Department shall order the county governments to collect all revenues in silver dollars and pay all expenditures in banknotes that have been restored to redemption, so that the banknotes issued by the Central Bank can circulate throughout the province. The implementation of these measures in each county will be determined by the Finance Department in an order. (8) Before each county government implements the measure of paying all expenditures in banknotes, the Central Bank should send personnel to the locations of the county governments to establish Central Bank redemption offices to facilitate the people's redemption. (9) After all Central Bank's banknotes have been fully restored to redemption, the Finance Department and the Special Envoy's Office should assess the situation and announce that all taxes and levies will still be collected in Central Bank's banknotes. It is reported that all national and provincial taxes in Guangdong Province will be collected in silver dollars from the 19th of this month in Guangzhou and from the date of receipt of the telegram in each county, and will still be collected with an additional 10% surcharge. However, the salt tax, tobacco tax, defense tax, Yihui money, land tax deed tax, and all Shatian income in Chaozhou, Meizhou, Qinzhou, and Lianzhou will still be collected in full silver dollars, without the 10% surcharge. (February 19th)

Increasing Revenue and Reducing Expenditure in Guangdong's Finances

Borrowing Guangzhou's Rentals for One Month

Deadline for Counties to Submit Fixed Grain Taxes

Administrative Expenses for Agencies Delayed for One Month

Guangzhou Correspondence: Recently, due to the urgency of Guangdong's finances and the need to maintain the financial system and replenish the Central Bank's capital, the Finance Department specially proposed borrowing one month's rentals from the entire city of Guangzhou. This was approved and implemented at the 56th Provincial Affairs Meeting on the 22nd. Yesterday, the Municipal Government was ordered to instruct the Public Security Bureau to expedite the process, with a deadline for collection within 20 days. The rent will be paid by the tenants on behalf of the landlords in silver dollars, and a receipt will be issued. After eight months, the landlords can take the receipt to the Central Bank to claim the borrowed cash. The regulations are as follows: (Article 1) The rent of one month will be borrowed from all shops, factories, temples, ancestral halls, guild halls, docks, and other buildings in Guangzhou, whether rented or self-occupied, for the purpose of reorganizing the financial system. The Guangdong Provincial Government shall order the Guangzhou Public Security Bureau to borrow on behalf of the landlords in accordance with the previous rental donation methods, and the collected funds will be submitted to the Guangdong Finance Department's treasury for verification and collection. (Article 2) The amount of rent to be borrowed shall be based on the amount recorded in the latest rental donation registers of the Guangzhou Public Security Bureau and its branches. (Article 3) For rented properties, the borrowed rent shall be paid by the tenants on behalf of the landlords, and the receipts shall be handed over to the landlords to deduct the rent. (Article 4) The deadline for paying the borrowed rent is 20 days from the date of announcement and implementation. A surcharge of 10% will be added for each month overdue, up to a maximum of 100%. (Article 5) The borrowed rent shall be paid in silver dollars. If the rent is calculated in other currencies, it shall be converted to silver dollars according to the market price on the date of payment. (Article 6) Eight months after the date of payment, the receipts can be taken to the Central Bank to claim the cash at any time. (Article 7) The borrowed rent receipt shall be in duplicate, issued by the Guangdong Finance Department for use, with a serial number listed at the perforated edge, stating the amount of silver dollars paid and sealed with the Finance Department's seal. One copy shall be given to the payer, and the other copy shall be sent to the Finance Department for filing. (Article 8) Both copies of the borrowed rent receipt shall state the payer's name, street name, house number, amount of silver dollars paid, and date, and shall be signed and sealed by the person in charge. (Article 9) Those who have paid the borrowed rent shall be issued a long strip of paper stating that "This household has paid the borrowed rent for financial reorganization" and affixed to the door for identification. It is reported that the collection of this rental donation will begin on March 1st, and the estimated amount to be collected is approximately 600,000 to 700,000 yuan in cash. In addition, for fundraising, 20% of the administrative expenses of various agencies will be paid in military expenditure coupons from February, and political expenses will also be delayed. For example, the salary for the first half of January will be paid in February, and the salary for the second half of January will be paid in March, and so on. Regarding the grain taxes of each county, it is stipulated that the grain tax for the 19th year must be prepaid from March 1st, and the overdue grain taxes for the 17th and 18th years must be paid in full before February 30th to fund the military. Yesterday, the Finance Department also determined the amount of grain taxes to be prepaid by each county, with a deadline of ten days from the date of receipt of the order to raise and prepay the amount in full. The amount to be raised by each county is as follows: Shunde, Nanhai, and Zhongshan each 60,000 yuan, Dongguan, Panyu, and Xinhui each 50,000 yuan, Zengcheng, Sanshui, Taishan, Gaoyao, and Boluo each 20,000 yuan, Qingyuan 15,000 yuan, Huaxian, Sihui, Xinxing, Luoding, Qujiang, Yingde, and Huiyang each 10,000 yuan, Baoan, Enping, Kaiping, Wuchuan, Deqing, Guangning, Hepu, Gaoming, Yunfu, Yunan, and Longmen each 5,000 yuan, Conghua 4,000 yuan, Fogang, Fengchuan, Lechang, Renhua each 2,000 yuan, Chixi, Kaijian, Lianshan, Lianping, Lingshan, Qinxian, Fangcheng, Wanning, Ganen, Xinfeng, Nanao, Changjiang, Xuwen each 1,000 yuan, totaling approximately 600,000 yuan. (February 23rd)

Tang Dynasty Princess's Tomb in Xinyang Excavated

Five miles south of Liulin Town, Southern District of Xinyang, Henan Province, there is a Longzhu Spring Temple, an ancient temple from the Tang Dynasty. Next to the temple is a tomb from the Tang Dynasty. According to legend, during the flourishing period of Buddhism in the Tang Dynasty, a certain princess went to worship in the South China Sea, escorted by Yuchi Gong. She died of illness on the way and was buried there. Many treasures were buried with her. In front of the tomb, there is a green stone tablet with an inscription by Chu Suiliang on Yuchi Gong's construction and repair, and the handwriting is still discernible. (It is said that the tablet has now been hidden.) There are also stone tables and stone incense burners, and the old site of the stone walls is still there, which is quite imposing and is one of the ancient sites of Xinyang County.

Unexpectedly, Nie Daozun, the chairman of the Liulin Chamber of Commerce, Wei Hanqing, the village head of Liulin Village, Zheng Bingqing, the head of the People's Self-Defense Team, and Tu Baiqing, the secretary of the Chamber of Commerce, acting on orders from an unknown organization, suddenly went to excavate the tomb on November 27th of last year. The excavated treasures were not made public. According to news from the monks of Longquan Temple and the members of the Chamber of Commerce, there were various antiques, including gold Buddhas, gold tripods, gold stoves, gold chopsticks, gold bowls, pearl-shining bowls, treasure bottles, and cranes. There were also small porcelain temples and figures, as well as items that were black with green rust, the names of which were unknown.

The tomb was built with stone strips into a circular vault, about 14 to 15 feet deep, about 8 feet wide, and about 7 feet high. There were square urns in the walls, like windows, about 1 foot square. There was an urn hole in the back wall, about 2 feet square and about 1 foot deep, with a pottery temple inside. Outside the tomb door, on the left and right, there were stone windows of 5 feet square each. The left window has been excavated and destroyed, and the right window has not yet been excavated. The project is huge and extremely sturdy.

According to general opinion, the Princess's tomb is one of the ancient sites of Xinyang and has been carefully protected throughout the Tang, Song, Yuan, Ming, and Qing dynasties. It has preservation value in terms of ancient sites. Now, it has suddenly been excavated, which is a great pity.

Former Director of the Chinese Eastern Railway Arrives in Harbin

The Protagonist of the Sino-Russian Case

Actually Serves as Deputy Director

Harbin Correspondence on the 21st: Ye Musanoff, the central figure in the Sino-Russian dispute, who was dismissed and expelled from the Chinese Eastern Railway by the former authorities of the Chinese Eastern Railway on July 10th of last year, arrived in Harbin on the evening of the 19th, according to a telephone call from Suifenhe, saying that Ye Musanoff had come from Russia and passed through the station to Harbin. He was accompanied by Ye's family members and the Russian Jie Yixieer. Ye and others arrived in Harbin at 2:30 PM on the 20th. The Special Police Department specially dispatched a part of the armed security team to stand guard outside the station to maintain order, and the first section of the road police also worked overtime to guard the platform. Those who came to greet him included important figures from the Railway Bureau and the Soviet Union in Harbin, such as Director Rudeyi, Deputy Director Jiannisoff, Directors Danilievsky and Shenmanovsky, and various section chiefs, along with about four to five hundred other expatriates. On our side, Directors Li Shaogeng, Guo Fumin, and Shen Ruilin, Supervisor Liu Zerong, Chinese Deputy Director Guo Chongxi, Counselor Jin Ronggui of the Supervision Office, and Chinese section chiefs, totaling about thirty people, also came. After the train stopped, the welcoming Russians shouted "Long live!" Many of our authorities also勉强expressed their so-called welcome with smiles. Izmaylov, who came to greet him, got off first, followed by Ye, who took off his hat to thank the welcoming crowd and strode into the VIP room. After a short rest, he took a car to the Russian Consulate. In the evening at 7:00 PM, senior Russian officials of the Railway Bureau held a banquet at the Railway Club to welcome Ye. At about 1:00 PM on the 21st, Ye took a car to the Board of Directors, where all the directors greeted him. He was led into Izmaylov's office, and then a joint meeting of the directors and supervisors was convened. The chairman was acting Director Guo Fumin. In addition to the Russian directors, the Chinese directors present were Li Shaogeng, Supervisor Liu Zerong, and Supervisor Zhang Shu. Izmaylov then produced a letter from the Soviet Russian Transportation Committee appointing Ye Musanoff as the Deputy Director of the Chinese Eastern Railway and asked the Chinese side to agree. It was immediately passed, and Ye Musanoff was invited into the conference hall. When Ye entered, everyone raised their glasses to congratulate him. After a short discussion, he resigned and went to the Railway Bureau to summon the section chiefs of the Railway Bureau. Director Rudeyi introduced him, and the section chiefs all congratulated Ye. After Ye met with the staff at the Railway Bureau, he bid farewell and left.

After Ye Musanoff changed his title to Deputy Director of the Chinese Eastern Railway and came to Harbin to take office, the current members of the Board of Directors in Harbin include Li Shaogeng, Guo Fumin, Fan Qiguang, and Shen Ruilin from the Chinese side, and Ye Musanoff, Izmaylov, Shenmanovsky, and Dalilievsky from the Russian side, which is sufficient for the legal quorum. All the matters of the Chinese Eastern Railway itself are extremely complicated. The return of Director Mo Dehui to Harbin in the near future will allow for a discussion on whether the Chinese and Russian sides can work together happily, which will be decided at this meeting.

Zhang and Jin Talk About Disturbances in Jiangxi; Zhu and Mao Will Be Cleared Soon

Since the Communist bandits Zhu De and Mao Zedong have been causing disturbances in the three provinces of Fujian, Jiangxi, and Guangdong, the people have been displaced and suffered unspeakable pain. Recently, they have been severely wounded after repeated suppression by government troops. Yesterday, a reporter from the Daily News specifically visited Zhang Huizhan and Jin Handing, the division commanders in charge of suppressing the bandits, to inquire about the recent situation of the bandits. They were kind enough to answer as follows:

Zhang Huizhan said that since He and Ye's rebellion, the Communist bandits have spread in Jiangxi. Since I was ordered to lead troops to garrison in Jiangxi, I have supervised my troops and fought hard to suppress them in order to eliminate the people's suffering. In the past six months, large groups of Communist bandits have been gradually defeated, and the lost territories have been recovered. Just as we were clearing them up, Zhu and Mao took advantage of our weak forces and led the bandits to disturb eastern Jiangxi again, capturing Guangchang and occupying Ningdu as their base. After the Central Government dispatched the Tang Brigade to Jiangxi, together with the Zhu and Dai Brigades, they attacked and captured the bandit nests in the past few days, and the bandit troops have fled, so there is no need to worry about a threat in the heart. After investigating, Zhu and Mao's strength is only about 4,000 people. Wherever they go, the houses are destroyed, and the people hate them to the bone. The bandits are still wearing single clothes, and the soldiers are only given six yuan a month, including food. They lack bullets, and the bandits all deeply regret their actions and often flee. If a complete plan is decided upon and a large army is used to encircle and suppress them, their roots can be eradicated in the shortest possible time.

Jin Handing said that since I led my troops to garrison at the border between Fujian and Jiangxi to block and suppress Zhu and Mao, they have been greatly damaged by our army's repeated encirclement and suppression. According to my investigation in Fujian, Mao Zedong did die of illness in Longyan. Only Zhu De is left. I have followed the Central Government's order to assign a brigade to be commanded by Chairman Lu. However, the Communist bandits often avoid the strong and attack the weak. I believe that as long as the Central Government allocates the troops properly, the main focus of bandit suppression should not be on recovering lost territories but on eliminating the bandits' strength. They should be fought at any time and wiped out. The most difficult thing about bandit suppression is that when lost territories are recovered, the people are afraid of the bandits and flee together, and there is no way to raise supplies. This time, I came to Beijing not only to pay my respects to Chairman Chiang and report on the garrison situation but also to discuss thoroughly with Division Commander Zhang Huizhan and formulate a complete plan to eliminate the Zhu bandits in the shortest possible time.

Japan Strives to Invest in the South Seas

Intends to Seize Commercial Rights from Overseas Chinese and Replace Them

Japan's ambition for commercial rights in the South Seas is not a recent development. Since the implementation of the gold standard, its financial situation has greatly improved, increasing the possibility of foreign investment to a significant degree. As a result, major financial groups are vying to establish foreign investment plans. The most noteworthy of these is the activity of the Oriental Development Company. This company, with its quasi-official nature, has a remarkable history in Japanese colonization. Having already acquired 7/30 of the land in the Korean Peninsula and invested tens of millions of yuan in Manchuria, it has in recent years adopted a southward advance policy, striving to develop its influence in the South Seas. With the recent implementation of the gold standard, it is now implementing two plans: "South Seas Investment" and "Subsidizing South Seas Cultivation." These plans were originally formulated by the current Minister of Finance, Masaji Inoue. Inoue is a man of great vision and foresight. During his time out of office, he visited various ports in the South Seas for on-the-spot investigations. Upon returning to Japan, he submitted these plans to the Oriental Development Company, urging them to implement them as soon as possible. However, due to various obstacles, the plans were never carried out. Now that the gold standard issue has been resolved, and the original planner is in a prominent position, the talk of South Seas investment is finally becoming a reality. In recent years, the commerce of overseas Chinese in the South Seas has gradually declined due to various factors. The impact of Japanese southward expansion is a significant reason for this decline. If we do not strive to resist it, the commercial rights that our overseas Chinese compatriots have held in the South Seas for hundreds of years will inevitably be lost completely. The following is a summary of Inoue's plans for "South Seas Investment" and "Subsidizing South Seas Cultivation" for the reference of those concerned about South Seas commerce.

(1) It is planned to establish a branch of the company in Singapore in the first half of next year, and also set up branches in major areas of the South Seas.

(2) The objects of investment are cultivation businesses such as rubber and tea. The purpose is to provide financing to assist Japanese enterprises.

(3) From next year, the investment will be set at 50 million yuan over ten years. 20 million yuan is currently prepared for investment.

(4) The total amount of Japanese investment in various parts of the South Seas is currently 70 million yuan. The funds provided by the Chinese Merchants Bank and the Bank of Taiwan amount to 8 million yuan. The Oriental Development Company plans to lend at low interest rates.

Local Correspondence

Kunshan

A Large Gang of Lake Bandits Gathered on the Shores of Cheng Lake, Not Far from Wucheng Tan Village, in the Bacheng District of Kunshan County

Yang Santai Temple, located three li away from the village on the lake surface, has a strategically important position. It's surrounded by the lake on three sides (the northeastern part of Yangcheng Lake), and the rear is a labyrinth of branching ports. The grass and forests form a rather dangerous terrain. The area currently belongs to Xiangcheng District of Wu County, connecting with Bacheng District of Kunshan County. An examination of the structure of Yang Santai Temple reveals it to be a five-bay, three-courtyard structure. The middle part has been covered in mud and dust, rarely visited by people, with only an old man guarding it. Therefore, robbers and thieves frequent the place from time to time. Recently, a large group of lake bandits arrived there, occupying the temple and holding several hostages on boats. It is said that the bandits have powerful firearms and appear and disappear unpredictably. They often post sentries at night, as far as ten li away, with flashing electric torches. The villagers are afraid to go out. The leader's surname is Wang, and the general firearms depot is in Yangcheng Village, in the Dianjing District of Wu County. (This place is also a hiding place for bandits in Yangcheng Lake.) It is said that the bandits have made elaborate arrangements, stationing five or six bandit boats at each strategically important port to prepare for any eventuality. However, the boats are quite diverse, including small fishing boats, farm boats, and speedboats. The food supply is transported by two dedicated boats, so there is no shortage of supplies. Large quantities of fish, meat, vegetables, tobacco, alcohol, oil, and firewood are purchased from Xiaojing Town in Xiangcheng District of Wu County. In recent days, Weijing Tang and Wu Jing in Wu County have been looted. It is also heard that the bandits have joined forces in Yangcheng Lake. Rumors are spreading that the bandits are planning to attack Xiangcheng, Dongtang, and Bacheng. Therefore, the head of the Ninth District of Kunshan County, Bacheng District, has requested and obtained eighty or ninety public security officers from the county government to patrol the countryside day and night.

Jiading

Carpenters and Bricklayers Gather to Discuss Price Increases

Local carpenters and bricklayers, due to the rising cost of living, have found that the originally agreed wages are insufficient. They gathered at the Luban Temple business association on the 23rd. As a result, they resolved to increase the price by six cents per worker, making it sixty cents per worker, effective from the beginning of June.

Dispute over Towel Tax Collection

The towel tax in this county has been contracted to Mao Yongji of the same industry, with a monthly amount of 120 yuan. Last year, Wu Gongyuan, Ma Zhengchang, Lu Yongyuan, Liu Zuting, and others contracted the tax in the name of the Towel Industry Merchants Association, increasing the amount to 180 yuan. They levied the tax on each loom operator at 1.2 yuan per load. Later, after members of the industry discovered fraudulent activities, they filed a complaint with the county party headquarters for investigation. This year, the tax collection was contracted to a newly formed Towel Industry Branch of the Merchants Association, which charges 80 cents per load. Wu Gongshun, Ma Zhengchang, Liu Zuting, and others, who originally handled the tax collection, were unwilling to accept this and, using the name of the old Towel Industry Merchants Association, secretly contracted the tax to the Chenjiadu sub-bureau and obtained tax forms from the Finance Department, which they distributed to the various members of the industry. At the beginning of the month, the first two shifts of boats transporting goods to Shanghai were allowed to pass. This was discovered by Chen Yisan, the executive director of the Towel Branch, who contacted the Shanghai Special Cotton Tax Bureau and obtained permission to cancel Wu Gongshun's contract. Recently, Daquanren, Wu Gongshun, Yichangyong, and others transported more than forty pieces of towels on Xu Shousheng's boat but did not report the tax. Chen Yisan of the Towel Branch requested the Nanxiang water police to detain the boat. The county chamber of commerce mediated, but no satisfactory agreement was reached. Daquanren and others believed that they were reporting the tax with a receipt and were not violating the law. The Towel Branch believed that since they had contracted the tax, they had the absolute right to dispose of it. The matter is currently at a standstill.

Songjiang

Resolution of Labor-Management Dispute at Cloth Factory

The weaving industry in this city has recently developed gradually. Major players in this industry, such as Xilin Cloth Factory and Guanghua Cloth Factory, experienced difficulties due to sluggish sales last year and repeated labor disputes. The factory owners all felt difficulties. They once announced a temporary shutdown in November of last year. Later, at the request of the workers' union, the county government mediated, and the factory owners reluctantly agreed to resume operations. By the end of last year, both Xilin and Guanghua factories reported losses. The Guanghua shareholders did not want to continue operating. After the accountant proved that the losses were real, they petitioned the county government to decide to close the factory. However, the workers claimed that the factories were destroying the labor movement and made several demands that the factory owners could not accept. Finally, the county government and the labor union mediated repeatedly and persuaded the workers. After several consultations, Xilin Cloth Factory agreed to pay each worker 15 yuan in severance pay, and Guanghua Factory agreed to pay each worker 16 yuan, with female workers receiving 3 to 4 yuan each. The factories submitted a list of workers to the county government for distribution and receipt. The workers have now left Songjiang to seek other employment.

Wuxi

Hidden Worries about the Future of the People's Food Supply

Since the beginning of spring in this county, the price of rice has risen sharply. The price of high-quality white rice has risen to 15.2 yuan per stone. The reason for the high price of rice is due to unscrupulous merchants transporting it for export. It was recently heard that several rice shops transported a total of 760 stones of rice to Nantong and Chongming in a few days. There are also many others that are not known to the public. Moreover, the sources of rice and wheat are also very scarce everywhere. An investigation in this county reveals that there are only over 100,000 stones of rice left. Even if this is used to supply the people in the county, it will only last until around April 15. If it continues to be transported for export, this county will be in danger of starvation. Yesterday, it was heard that County Magistrate Sun plans to convene a meeting of rice industry leaders in the next few days to discuss and strictly prohibit exports to maintain the people's food supply.

The Department of Civil Affairs Orders Private Purchase of Firearms

The Department of Civil Affairs believes that in recent years, banditry has been rampant in various parts of Jiangsu Province. It has been suppressed repeatedly but continues to rise. Various counties are mostly purchasing firearms for self-defense as a precaution. However, firearms are a major concern, and carelessness in handling them can lead to abuses. Previous regulations on the purchase of firearms have been issued to the counties for compliance. However, recently some counties have purchased firearms without prior approval, which is inappropriate. Therefore, the previous order was reiterated yesterday. In the future, any purchase of firearms should be based on the county's consideration of the situation, with a list of types and quantities, submitted to the department for approval in advance before preparing the funds and reporting to the department for handling on their behalf.

In addition to the county government's approved request to the provincial government to allocate 2,000 yuan per month from the self-government house tax in Zhenyi, yesterday it also issued an order to each district that all miscellaneous taxes and property rents should be distributed equally by the Funds and Property Office in the future.

Puji Ferry Delayed Indefinitely

The Puji ferry from Zhenjiang to Guazhou Shierxu was originally built with public donations and is entirely charitable in nature. However, due to poor management, although the ferry tickets are sold at the listed price, the revenue and expenditure still cannot be offset. The ferry has been suspended for nearly a month and has not yet resumed operations. Travelers from Zhenjiang, Jiangdu, and Yizheng Counties are extremely inconvenienced. It is said that the reason for this is that the distribution of duties by one or two officials has not been determined, causing this charitable ferry to be suspended for a long time. There is now talk of holding a committee meeting on March 1, but it is unknown how it will be resolved.

Yangzhou

Request for Assistance in Collecting Rice Tax Outside the South Gate

The members of the Rice Tax Collection Committee in this county, Ye Yuqing, etc., believe that due to the famine in the northwest countryside in the eighteenth year, 80-90% of the rice shops in Situ Temple, Fenghuang Qiaoqiao, and other places have successively closed down, resulting in a sharp decline in tax revenue. The only reliable source of revenue now is a small area by the South Gate River, where business is still strong. Based on previous precedents and collection methods, they are investigating the detailed accounts of each household's transactions to verify the collection, in order to offset the losses with gains. Yesterday, they specially requested the county government to instruct Cao Bingnan, the chief of the rice industry, and Li Ziheng and Yang Zazhi, the directors outside the South Gate, to assist in handling the case, recover the old debts, and rectify the new tax. It is heard that the county has approved the request.

Daylight Robbery in Denglong Lane

Wang, the former Director of Finance during the tenure of Prefect Zhang, resided in Denglong Lane in this county. On the 26th, at around 1:00 PM, three men dressed in suits and carrying pistols suddenly entered the house and robbed it, while guarding the gate. Even the person collecting donations for cleaning was given a donation of one corner of the ocean for guarding the gate before closing the gate again. After the robbery, the robbers locked the door and left by car, passing through Sanzhu An and heading east. Afterwards, the victim checked and found that the losses amounted to about 800 yuan, including a male fox fur robe, three male and female sheepskin robes, four gold hairpins, and a set of earrings, with the rest being cash. The matter was immediately reported to the Second Sub-Bureau in charge for investigation. It was later heard that the robbers had taken a certain ship to Gaoyou, and the Second Sub-Bureau in charge was telegraphed to investigate. It was also heard that when the robbers hailed the car, they said they were going to Dongguan. An investigation revealed that they had boarded the Yangyou bus heading north. The Public Security Bureau has telephoned the Shaobo Public Security Bureau to conduct a thorough inspection when the ship arrives at the port. It is unknown whether they will be able to apprehend the robbers.

Qingjiang

Joint Defense Meeting

The Thirteenth Brigade Headquarters of this port convened a joint defense meeting on the afternoon of the 23rd at 3:00 PM, inviting representatives from various agencies, including Xu Jiaqing, the County Magistrate of Huaiyin, Yang Tie of the Public Security Bureau, etc. The meeting was chaired by Wei Rucheng, Chief of Staff of the Brigade. Various resolutions were passed. Due to the current unstable situation and the tense defense situation, the resolutions will be kept secret for the time being. However, regarding the defense of the city and the maintenance of law and order, in addition to the local armed groups strengthening patrols, the supplementary battalion of the Thirteenth Brigade will also be stationed in Pu to guard the area.

Bandits Kidnapped a Child

Several bandits arrived at the home of Guo Can in Guozhuang, near Xujialiu in the northern countryside, and robbed all the guns. They also took away Guo's third son, Xiao Sanzi. Upon hearing the news, the local village militia went out to rescue the child, and one bandit even opened fire on them. After about an hour, they fled to the north.

Nantong

Six Counties' Bandit Suppression Conference Held in Ju Tai

Communist bandits in the six counties of Jiangbei, Nantong, Taixian, Rugao, Jingjiang, Dongtai, and Taixing, colluded and caused disturbances. The Department of Civil Affairs, on the order of the provincial government, instructed the county magistrates of the six counties to earnestly discuss measures to suppress the bandits and submit them for approval. It has now ordered the County Magistrate of Taixian to be the director of the preparatory committee for the joint defense conference of the six counties, scheduling a meeting in Ju Tai and ordering the county magistrates to attend the meeting on time to discuss and report for approval.

Police Dispatched to Shanghai to Extradite Bandit Leader

The bandit leader Zhuang Dianchen from Jiangbei committed robbery and murder in the county. He was arrested in Shanghai and sent to the Temporary Court. Knowing that the Nantong County Government was well aware of this, County Magistrate Chen dispatched police with a letter to Shanghai to extradite him back to the county for interrogation.

Jiangbei Counties Continue to Recruit Laborers to Build Roads

The counties of Tongru, Taihai, and others in Jiangbei, on the order of the Department of Construction, are continuing to recruit laborers to expand and build roads. From now on, the construction bureaus of each county will recruit laborers to build roads according to the routes set by the province.

Fundraising to Repair Prisons

Warden Yu of the Fourth Prison in Tongcheng, together with County Magistrate Chen, invited representatives from local groups to form a committee to raise funds to repair the prisons and detention centers, soliciting donations from all walks of life.

The County Conducts a Thorough Clearing Campaign

Tongyi is conducting a thorough clearing campaign, dividing the county into six major districts, each with a sub-bureau. The directors have been recommended by the district chiefs and will all start on March 1.

平湖

Xu Zhengming Dies of Illness in Prison: Xu Zhengming, a resident of Pinghu known for his fierceness, had previously schemed to kill a distant uncle, Mr. Jia, over a certain matter. He was imprisoned and sentenced to ten years by the county government. Recently, he died of illness in prison. Upon receiving the news, his family came to the city yesterday to request exemption from an autopsy. After being permitted by the authorities, they hired a boat to transport the body back to his home, where they proceeded with the burial arrangements.

Conflict Among Patrol Unit Leaders: Tao, a member of the Xin Cang Patrol Unit, lost a wooden-cased gun a few days ago. The platoon leader, Lin Xia, reported this to the deputy commander, Xu, who ordered an interrogation. However, no leads were found. Deputy Commander Xu then offered a reward for information leading to its recovery. In reality, Tao's gun had been hidden by platoon leader Dai. The following morning, Dai falsely claimed to have found it in an ash pile in the back garden and intended to claim the reward. Lin Xia discovered this and secretly reported the details to Deputy Commander Xu. Xu was enraged, reprimanded Dai, and suggested he resign. Afterward, Dai became angry with Lin and wanted to fight him. Other patrol members intervened to separate them. Still unwilling to let it go, Dai went to the provincial security team stationed in the town, incited several fellow villagers, and armed themselves. They found Lin Xia in the Guandi Temple and attacked him as a group, causing chaos and panic in the town. Eventually, officers from both sides intervened to stop the fight, and platoon leader Dai was temporarily detained at the public security bureau, bringing the incident to an end.

Theft Reported in Xiaoqiao Village: In Xiaoqiao Village, about six miles from this city, the home of resident Sun A'da was targeted by over twenty robbers late on the 25th. Armed with knives and clubs, they broke down the door and ransacked the house, stealing all the clothing, jewelry, silver, and other valuables, resulting in a loss of over five hundred yuan. The case has been reported to the county government for a thorough investigation.

[P Huzhou >

Robbery on Jiahu Steamboat en Route: On the 23rd, the "Flying Dragon" small steamboat, traveling from Jiaxing to Huzhou and towing a vessel from the Huali Company along with a patrol boat from the 13th Water Police Unit, encountered robbers at Anfeng, a gambling spot where the borders of Wuzhen and Shuanglin meet. At around 5 PM, five bandits had already hidden on the Huali Company's vessel. One bandit went to the bow of the boat and fired a shot into the air. Suddenly, three bandit boats approached, and over twenty bandits armed with wooden-cased guns swarmed onto the steamboat. Over a dozen water police officers on the towed patrol boat were about to grab their guns to defend themselves, but the bandits fired at them, killing one and wounding another. The bandits also seized eight wooden-cased guns from the patrol boat. Seeing the ferocity of the attack, the water police officers jumped into the water to escape. The bandits, seeing the water police had fled, swarmed into the Huali Company's vessel, searching it at will. None of the passengers escaped unscathed. Before leaving, they kidnapped a paper shop owner from Wuzhen and the chairman of the Wuzhen Chamber of Commerce, Mr. Shen. The bandits remained on the boat for about an hour before firing several shots and fleeing in small boats. The steamboat arrived at its destination late at night. The losses amounted to over three thousand yuan.

Death from Beating over Gambling Debt: Yang Shunyuan, a resident of Zhuangyuanfang in the South Street of this city, demanded one yuan in gambling money from Yao Sanmai, who lived with him, on the 18th of this month. This led to an argument and then a physical fight. Yao's mother-in-law and wife joined in the beating for some time. Neighbors heard the noise and went upstairs to mediate, but Yang Shunyuan had already suffered injuries to his head and waist. Yang's wife helped him home. In the evening, he vomited blood several times. At around 2 AM on the 20th, he suffered severe abdominal pain and died. The local bailiff, Xu Changshou, and the deceased's brother, Yinbao, mediated a settlement. Yao Sanbao issued a promissory note for thirty yuan to settle the matter. However, the deceased's cousin, Shen, learned of this and reported it to the Wuxing Court. On the 22nd, Prosecutor Wang arrived at the scene with officials to conduct an autopsy. The body was examined and showed no injuries. However, when the body was turned over, the blood that the deceased vomited was taken to the court for testing. At that time, Prosecutor Wang ordered that the body be placed in a coffin within an hour and a half. Yesterday, the deceased's wife went to the court again to request a second autopsy.

Jiashan

Grand Theft at Wuhua Store: The Wuhua Department Store on the main street in Jiashan was targeted by thieves last night around the third watch of the night. They pried open the back door and stole various goods worth about a thousand yuan. A list of stolen items has been submitted to the county Public Security Bureau for investigation.

Public Security Bureau Continues to Capture Kidnappers: After the Jiashan County Public Security Bureau previously captured accomplices to a kidnapping, Wu Jinrong and Sheng Agui, they confessed that there were other accomplices scattered in the eastern townships. Yesterday, the county Public Security Bureau dispatched a team and captured five people in the Yaozhuang Bridge, Hengjing, and Fengjing areas. They have been taken to the county for interrogation.

Jiaxing

Robbery with Injury in Hantang District: A farmer named Afu in the Tongzihang area of Hantang District, Jiaxing, had some savings. One night recently, several robbers suddenly arrived, openly carrying weapons, and broke down the door. The housewife heard the commotion and fled out the door, but was spotted by the robbers, who struck her head with a weapon. The woman immediately collapsed to the ground, bleeding profusely. The robbers then rushed into the inner room, looting at will. They left with a whoop after about an hour. Upon inspection afterward, it was found that clothes and various items had been stolen, with unspecified losses. The injured woman has been sent to the He Hospital for treatment.

Commercial School Discovers Epidemic and Suspends Classes: The Jiaxing County Commercial Vocational School discovered cases of meningitis and diphtheria on the afternoon of the 25th. Principal Wang Zhongxiang, considering that these epidemics are highly contagious, telegraphed the Education Bureau and received permission to suspend classes temporarily for four days, starting on the 26th. All students were notified to return home so that the school could carry out various disinfection procedures. Classes will resume as usual on March 3rd.

Preparatory Meeting for Tree Planting Campaign: The Yin County government convened a preparatory meeting for the tree planting campaign in memory of Dr. Sun Yat-sen yesterday afternoon at 1 PM. Representatives from various organizations attended. The meeting decided that the tree planting location would be at Dongqian Lake, and the tree planting ceremony would be held at Zhifang Elementary School.

Mayor Luo Goes to Cixi to Recuperate: Ningbo Mayor Luo Huiqiao has requested to resign due to illness. All duties have been delegated to Xu Zhun as acting mayor. Luo himself left by car for Baoguo Temple in Cixi yesterday morning at 9 AM to recuperate.

Citywide Sports Meet Scheduled: The city public sports field plans to hold a citywide sports meet on March 6th, as the National Games are about to open and there is an urgent need to select talent to participate in the grand event. Preparations are actively underway.

Letter Received

Letter from the Ministry of Interior

Recently, I read in your newspaper's "Important News" section that the Ministry of Interior is drafting regulations on wedding and funeral rites. This does not entirely align with the facts. The Ministry's Department of Rites and Customs submitted a request last November to organize a rites and customs drafting committee, and various committee members were appointed to carry out the work. Several drafts have been prepared, but they are still under review and have not been passed by the general assembly. The statement that they have been submitted to the Executive Yuan for review is not factual. This letter is to clarify and request a correction. Ministry of Interior, February 25th.

Education News

Important News

Ministry of Education Explains Regulations on Academic Organizations

The Ministry of Education, based on a report from the Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau regarding various academic organizations affiliated with national, provincial, municipal, and private schools at all levels, or various academic organizations organized by teachers and students of these schools that use the school's name but are privately run in nature, and which were originally approved by the schools or higher-level education authorities or are supervised and guided by the schools, seeks clarification on whether such quasi-public and quasi-private academic organizations should be managed by local education administrative agencies. The Ministry instructed the bureau, stating that if various academic organizations established by public and private schools use the school's name and their membership is limited to teachers and students of the school, they may be managed by the school itself. However, other academic organizations affiliated with the schools that allow external members should be managed in accordance with the regulations of the education administrative agency for academic organizations. The order is issued to the bureau for compliance and dissemination. [P Ministry of Education's Letter to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs >

Regarding the International Conference on Applied Science

The Ministry of Education sent a letter to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs regarding the dispatch of representatives to attend the Third International Conference on Applied Science in Sweden. The letter stated that the Ministry had approved a letter from the Swedish Embassy informing that the Third International Conference on Applied Science was scheduled to be held in Stockholm and inviting the Chinese government and public and private experts to send representatives to attend. The letter and enclosed invitation and registration forms were forwarded for review and response. The Ministry stated that the government should send personnel and that the Ministry would revise the term "science" to "mechanical engineering" in the original text. The letter and attachments were forwarded to the Academia Sinica for consideration and action, and instructions were sent to universities, colleges, and academic organizations with a strong focus on mechanical engineering to report to the Ministry if they wished to attend the conference for further action.

Zhejiang Education Department Specifies Procedures for Implementing Secondary Education

The Zhejiang Education Department has finalized its plan for implementing secondary education in the province and will proceed in accordance with the specified procedures. The plan includes: (1) Formulating key points for secondary education; (2) Drafting methods to promote continuing education for in-service teachers and staff; (3) Drafting methods to enhance students' interest in learning; (4) Promoting and guiding the status of teaching methodology; (5) Ordering all secondary schools to add health instructors or committees; (6) Piloting vocational and college guidance; (7) Investigating the status of science education and seeking to increase its efficiency; (8) Promoting the application of high school testing methods; (9) Planning for the separate construction of provincial school buildings; (10) Continuing to reorganize municipal, county, and private secondary schools; (11) Revising the supplementary regulations for the registration of junior high schools; (12) Revising the methods for subsidizing students with provincial funds. [P Zhejiang Education Department Submits a Request to the Ministry of Education to Promulgate Regulations on Educational Professionalization >

and Protection Regulations for Elementary Education Personnel

The Zhejiang Education Department submitted a document to the Ministry of Education yesterday, stating that the Third Zhejiang Provincial Third School District Education Administrative Personnel Joint Conference reported that the cultivation of talent, mining, medicine, and education are distinct fields. Originally, the purpose was to cultivate specialized talent for the development of various industries. However, in recent years, it has become common for those who study medicine to engage in commerce, and those who study agriculture to engage in law. This is especially prevalent in the education sector, to the extent that those who fail to succeed in other fields use the education sector as a haven, and those who lose their jobs use the education sector as a refuge. The education sector is seen as unimportant and accessible to everyone, which is unfortunate for the education sector. Therefore, for the sake of developing and emphasizing education, it is recommended to request the Ministry of Education to promulgate regulations on educational professionalization and protection regulations for elementary education personnel for compliance. According to this, it is common for elementary education personnel to leave their posts during their term of office or for other reasons, and it is true that unemployed people use education as a refuge. The promulgation of regulations on educational professionalization and protection regulations for elementary education personnel seems to be urgently needed today. The report presents the above situation and requests review and implementation.

Zhejiang Education Department Inspectors Depart for Inspection

And Sends Specialists to Inspect Vocational and Normal Education

Chen, the Director of the Zhejiang Education Department, believes that since elementary schools in the province have already started, it is imperative to dispatch inspectors for inspection to seek improvement. It was decided to dispatch eight inspectors, with one remaining in the department for office work. The rest were scheduled to depart on March 14th to inspect forty counties divided into five routes, excluding those already inspected in the previous session. Shen Qi will lead the first route, covering ten counties including Fuyang. Feng Keshu will lead the second route, covering eight counties including Mayen. Chen Zhang will lead the third route, covering seven counties including Xinchang. Zhang Rentian will lead the fourth route, covering eight counties including Tonglu. Lu Guqing will lead the fifth route, covering seven counties including Xuanping. Director Chen also believes that the province lacks resources and vocational education lacks a foundation. To investigate the truth and seek improvement, Zhu Wenzhi was appointed to inspect the normal education department or normal training classes and affiliated elementary schools of provincial secondary schools, as well as county and city private normal training institutions. Qian Jiazhi was appointed to inspect various vocational schools and revisit the provincial, county, and city private secondary schools already inspected in the previous session. Zhang Xingjian will remain in the department for office work.

Status of the 17th Academic Year Graduates of National Central University

The National Central University has held four graduation ceremonies since its reorganization, graduating over 700 students. Most are now serving the party and the country. Excluding nine who stayed to study, five who continued academic research, and one who died, ten served in party affairs, twenty-three in the industrial sector, twenty as government officials, two as journalists, and one hundred and forty-one as teachers and staff. Implementation of Increased Tuition Fees: Suzhou's educational funding has reached a critical point. The mayor decided to increase tuition fees and submitted a request to the Education Department for approval. The Education Department has approved the request. This semester, junior elementary tuition will be increased to two yuan and senior elementary to four yuan. However, the actual situation in the schools is that the number of students has decreased compared to before the increase, and the number of students has also been slightly affected. The municipal government still has no solution in terms of funding, and the salaries for January have not yet been paid.

[ Municipal Education Bureau Orders Revision of Temporary Standards for Secondary School Curriculum

The Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau issued an order to all municipal secondary schools and registered private secondary schools regarding the forwarding of the revised key points of the temporary standards for the secondary school curriculum, stating that the bureau previously hired personnel to organize a primary and secondary school curriculum research committee to carefully study the standards required by the Ministry of Education in accordance with the local needs and environmental conditions of the city. It democratically decided on the types of subjects and weekly time allocation for elementary schools in the city and ordered all elementary schools to comply and conduct trials. Now, it has also been agreed to revise the temporary standards for the secondary school curriculum. The key points for revision have been approved by the bureau's meeting and will be sent to each secondary school for a one-semester trial. The results of the trial should be reported for filing. The revised key points are copied and issued for compliance. This order.

Key Points for Revising Temporary Standards for Secondary School Curriculum

1. A clause on Chinese indigenous culture should be added to the Chinese language teaching syllabus for junior high school. 2. Chinese history and foreign history should be taught separately to emphasize national evolution. 3. Grammar and reading materials for English teaching may be separated as appropriate. 4. One credit should be added to the integrated science subject, making it two hours of teaching. 5. According to the Ministry's regulations, four hours of musical instrument practice should be held weekly starting from the first grade of junior high school. If it is difficult to implement due to the relationship between time and musical instruments, singing may be substituted. 6. The extraction of square roots and calculation of area in junior high school arithmetic should be deleted, and teaching materials and time should be added to the extraction of square roots in algebra and the area of geometry. 7. Abacus calculation does not need to be listed as a separate elective subject, and abacus calculation and written calculation should be listed separately in the four operations of integers in arithmetic. 8. Teaching methods for junior high school arithmetic should focus on the distinction between numbers and quantities. 9. Insert "Exponent One" between power and root extraction and factorization in junior high school algebra, and add "Two" under the original words "teaching". 10. A system of two quadratic equations in two variables should be added after rational and radical equations in junior high school algebra. 11. Trigonometry in the fourth semester of senior high school should be changed from two credits to three credits.
