All students from municipal schools in South Shanghai and Zhabei, except for schools that are closer and can go directly to the venue, must gather at the First Stadium before 12 noon on that day, and the preparation committee will provide transportation to the venue, etc. According to this, there are slight changes from the previous resolution of the committee. In addition to separate orders, all schools are hereby ordered to comply. This order.

[P Railway Expert Returning from England >

Mr. Kuang Kaihua (Meng Hou), a native of Xiangshan, Guangdong, graduated from Tsinghua School in 1925. In the autumn of that year, he went to the United States and entered Ohio University, specializing in vehicle management and commercial port management, and obtained a bachelor's degree. He then worked in the freight department of the Chicago Railway for one year. Later, he was hired by the Union Pacific Railroad Bureau as an assistant to the general section chief. In the autumn of the 18th year of the Republic, he went to England and entered the graduate school of the University of London, specializing in railway finance. In the same year, he was recommended as a member of the Royal Society of Transportation in the United Kingdom. Cai Zengji, the Minister of Railways of our country, believes that Mr. Kuang has both knowledge and experience in railway administration and strongly urged him to return to China. Mr. Kuang has now arrived in Shanghai and will go to Beijing soon. He may work in the Ministry of Railways in the future.

Four Singles and One Doubles

Since Wu Bangwei took over the competition division of the National Games Organizing Committee, he has formulated the rules for various ball games separately. Xinzi Group Wins Newspaper Workers' Football Championship

Two Goals to Zero Victory Over the Current Affairs Group

The Newspaper Workers' Football Championship competition results have been recorded in this newspaper several times. Yesterday morning at 10:00 AM, the Xinzi Group played against the Shizi Group. Both teams' athletes bravely and willingly exerted themselves for a long time, neither yielding to the other. Later, the Xinzi Group's center forward took advantage of a gap and attacked, the goalkeeper pounced and hit the ball right onto the body of the right forward, who then put it into the net. The Xinzi Group opened the scoring first. Later, the Shizi Group's left inside forward received a ball and, judging the ball's momentum accurately, headed it, but it landed in front of the Xinzi Group's goal and was saved by the inside back. In the first half, the Xinzi Group took the lead with a score of 1 to 0. Afterwards, the Shizi Group counterattacked with all its strength, the center forward received the ball and shot at the goal, but all shots missed. Despite repeated attempts to retaliate, they were unsuccessful. The Xinzi Group scored another goal within ten minutes due to being too eager. After that, there was no more progress on either side. As a result, the Xinzi Group won with a score of 2 to 0, and the Xinzi Group won the championship with six points. The referee was Mr. He Chunhui.

Women's Basketball Uses Men's Rules

The Chinese National Sports Promotion Association recently received an official reply from the secretariat of the Japan Sports Association, stating that the basketball and baseball games for women's performance in the Games will adopt the newly established men's rules of the United States from 1929 to 1930 as the standard. It has been found that women's basketball in our country, in Shanghai, has always used the latest two-zone American rules, and other places also use two-zone rules. However, only Guangdong Fangxu uses men's rules. If the women's team in our country wants to participate in Japan this time, Shanghai and other places must pay attention to it. Because the National Games is also a preliminary round for the Far Eastern Games, it seems necessary to discuss the rules for women's basketball.

Yesterday's Gold Price Soared Again

Highest 504 Taels

Closing Price 501 Taels 1 Mace

Yesterday morning, the price of silver in Europe fell to a new low, and the local foreign exchange market was very weak. The listed prices were all historically low. Speculators rushed to buy gold pounds and gold foreign currency, and banks were unwilling to sell them, causing the price of gold to rise to 504 taels at a certain time in the morning, setting a new record. The price fell slightly in the afternoon, but the closing price was still 501 taels and 1 mace.

Foreign Steamships Increase Freight Again

To be Implemented Starting Tomorrow

During the low-water period last winter on the Changsha route in the upper reaches of the Yangtze River, when Chinese ships were suspended, foreign ships such as Taikoo, Nissin, and Jardine increased the freight by one-fold. By early February of this year, the water level rose slightly, and Chinese ships resumed operation, so the foreign companies reduced the added freight. Now, because the Chinese merchant ships on this route have stopped operating one after another, foreign ships such as Taikoo are once again taking advantage of the opportunity, saying that the water level above Hankou has decreased again, and they are discussing increasing the freight by 50%. Yesterday, the companies had already agreed to implement the increase tomorrow. The freight per ton has increased from 5 taels and 4 mace to 8 taels and 1 mace. The minimum bill of lading has increased from 2 taels to 2 taels and 5 mace. Because the new freight rates for other goods are of great concern to Chinese merchants, a survey has been conducted and divided into one or two categories as follows: (All goods must first go to Hankou, so two batches of freight must be paid to reach Changsha.)

Sanbei Company's Flying Tiger Ship Sinks

The Branch Office Has Received a Telegram from Hankou

The Sanbei Company's Flying Tiger ship, which came to Shanghai from Vladivostok last winter, was dispatched to Nanjing and Hankou. Yesterday, the company received a telegram from its Hankou branch, reporting that the ship had been struck and sunk by a warship. The original telegram was very brief, stating that the Flying Tiger ship was at the China Merchants Bureau wharf in Hankou at noon yesterday (the 27th).

As the ship was being moved, it was violently struck amidships by a Chinese warship there. The hull of the Flying Tiger ship immediately broke open, and the river water rushed into the cabin, causing the ship to sink into the river. Within half an hour, the entire ship had sunk into the river. Fortunately, there was no cargo on board, and the crew members and sailors escaped to the China Merchants Bureau wharf during the accident, so there were no casualties. Details have not yet been reported. The Flying Tiger ship had a deadweight of more than 2,000 tons, and the total loss of the ship is more than 100,000 yuan. It is heard that the ship's hull was insured with marine insurance. After receiving the telegram yesterday, the bureau notified the insurance company for investigation.

Please Disclose the Full Text of the Sino-Japanese Reciprocal Agreement First

National Products Factory Union Sends Telegram to the Government

The Shanghai National Products Factory Union telegraphed the National Government Executive Yuan and the Ministries of Foreign Affairs, Finance, Industry, and Commerce yesterday, stating that reports indicate that all issues in the Sino-Japanese tariff negotiations have been resolved and that the treaty will be signed soon. Regarding the reciprocal agreement, Japan has proposed more than 100 items such as cotton yarn and cotton cloth, all of which are industrial re-products. The reciprocal tariff items that our country imports from Japan are mostly raw materials, and the number is not as large as Japan's. Reading it is quite astonishing. It is undeniable that our country's industry is backward and commerce is sluggish. Japan has numerous factories and very rich products, which are sold in large quantities to our country. Examining the recent customs trade booklets, the comparison between raw material exports and product imports is far apart. To plug the leaks, increasing taxes is not enough, so how can they be included in reciprocity? Reciprocity means that each side is mutually beneficial. Now, exchanging raw materials from backward industries for products from developed industries is beneficial to Japan and harmful to us, and is not reciprocity, but cutting ourselves with a knife. If the reports are true, it will greatly hinder the future of promoting national products. At a time when national products factories are struggling, if their products are allowed to be included in reciprocity, it will be tantamount to cutting off their own lifeblood. What is felt to be dangerous cannot be kept silent, so a special telegram is sent to request that the full text of the agreement be disclosed before it is signed so that it can be studied to avoid regrets. Lu Xingzhuang, Zhang Bingsen, Shen Mengshi, Xu Jianfan, and Ma Jisheng, standing committee members of the Shanghai National Products Factory Union, respectfully bow.

National General Chamber of Commerce Cables Request to Reduce Postal Rates for Overseas Chinese

The National General Chamber of Commerce cabled the National Government yesterday, stating: "To the esteemed Nanjing National Government: It has been found that the Ministry of Communications has ordered the cancellation of overseas Chinese letter offices in various locations. Henceforth, bulk mailings are prohibited, and each letter must be individually affixed with a stamp. We have repeatedly received reports from the subordinate associations and reports from the British Executive Committee, as well as letters and telegrams from the Shantou General Chamber of Commerce, requesting that we forward a telegram requesting the continuation of the old practices. We have accordingly cabled the Ministry of Communications, ordering the General Post Office to continue the old practices to alleviate the difficulties of the overseas Chinese. However, we have repeatedly received replies from the Ministry stating that since our country has joined the Universal Postal Union, the United Kingdom and the Netherlands are unwilling to send bulk mailings, and there is nothing that can be done. Now, upon reading a news item published in the Shanghai Shen Bao on February 26th, regarding the petition of overseas Chinese in Singapore for a reduction in postal rates, it is stated that the Governor of Singapore, the Chinese Affairs Commissioner, the Postmaster General, and others replied that this matter was not initiated by the British government, but was based on a letter from the Chinese government requesting the abolition of bulk mailings and a uniform increase in rates, and they presented various letters from the Chinese General Post Office, etc. After reading this, we are extremely dismayed. Our government daily declares its protection of overseas Chinese, but they have not received any actual benefits, and exploitation is rampant. The increase in postal rates and the abolition of bulk mailings are clear evidence of this. We hereby request that your esteemed government investigate and verify the matter, and immediately order the Executive Yuan to strictly order the Ministry of Communications and the General Post Office to immediately withdraw the order and continue the old practices, in order to safeguard the overseas Chinese. This would be a great act of kindness."

[P Postal Director-General Discusses the Issue of Bulk Mail Delivery by Nanyang Private Letter Offices]

The Postal Director-General of the local Ministry of Communications spoke in detail to a reporter from the Guomin News Agency yesterday regarding the issue of bulk mail delivery by Nanyang private letter offices. The following is a record of the discussion, for the reference of those concerned with overseas Chinese affairs. (The following is the Postal Director-General's statement): "In French Annam, American Philippines, Dutch East Indies, British Malayan Archipelago and Siam, there are many overseas Chinese from our country. Their communications with the mainland are mostly handled by private letter offices. The method of receiving and sending mail is to pack a large number of letters into a bulk package and send it as one item. When the bulk package arrives at its destination, it is received by the receiving private letter office, which then distributes the letters in the package to the recipients. In recent years, the postal administrations of various countries have protested to our country, requesting the abolition of this type of bulk package, as it conflicts with the Universal Postal Convention and their domestic regulations. Although we have repeatedly tried to deal with the situation, Annam, the Philippines, and Siam have successively implemented the abolition of bulk mailings. The Dutch postal administration has also repeatedly sent letters since 1925, requesting the abolition of bulk mailings. Our country's postal administration has always politely requested postponement. However, in August 1928, they sent letters and telegrams, firmly reiterating their previous proposal and refusing to make further concessions. Our country is a member of the Universal Postal Union and has an obligation to comply with the Universal Postal Convention. Since the Dutch postal administration has strictly enforced its domestic regulations based on the Universal Postal Convention and firmly rejected our requests, we have no way to force them to make concessions. We have reported this matter to the Ministry of Communications for record. Furthermore, in August 1929, the postal administration of Kuala Lumpur, British Malaya, sent a telegram stating that the governments of the Malayan Archipelago and the Nanyang Islands had decided to abolish the private letter office system and would implement it starting from January 1, 1930. While we were reviewing the matter, we received a letter from the Kuala Lumpur postal administration on September 2, reiterating their previous request and demanding the abolition of bulk mailings. Our country's postal administration repeatedly requested postponement and sent personnel to Xiamen and Shantou to discuss solutions with the relevant private letter offices, informing them of the situation and proposing appropriate solutions that comply with the Universal Postal Convention and the regulations of the British postal administration. The purpose was to ensure that communications for overseas Chinese would not be inconvenienced by the British postal administration's abolition of private letter offices, and that our country's postal administration would not be accused of violating the Universal Postal Convention. The facts are all there and can be reviewed. Now, a report states that the Governor of Singapore and the Postmaster General have presented letters from our bureau, stating that this matter was initiated by our government requesting the abolition of bulk mailings, which is contrary to the facts. We believe that the British authorities would not go so far as to reverse the truth. We have sent a telegram to question them and have submitted the entire case to the Ministry of Communications for review and handling, in order to clarify the truth. In short, our bureau has always taken the convenience of the public as its duty, and we will pay special attention to the convenience of overseas Chinese. This misunderstanding should be resolved soon."

Land Bureau Measures Household Land in Zhabei District

The Land Bureau issued a notice yesterday regarding the measurement of household land in the 27th Bao, 10th Tu of Zhabei District, stating: "Notice: The Bureau is now beginning to measure household land in the 27th Bao, 10th Tu of Zhabei District. Landowners should pay attention to the following: (1) The Dibao (local land officer) will distribute registration forms to the landowners. Landowners should fill them out accurately within ten days of receiving them and return them to the Dibao, who will collect them and submit them to the Zhabei Measurement Office of the Bureau at the Guanyin Temple in Xiajia, Qiujiang Road. (2) Landowners who do not receive a registration form because their address is unknown may directly contact the Bureau or the Measurement Office to fill one out. (3) Landowners whose land is pawned or mortgaged and cannot fill out the registration form with the name and mu (unit of area) should promptly copy the information from the pawnee or mortgagee and not make excuses. (4) When the household land is measured, the landowner must accompany the Dibao to clearly indicate the boundaries to the surveyor or pre-authorize a representative to indicate the boundaries on-site. Otherwise, the Bureau will only rely on the Dibao's instructions, and the landowner will be responsible for any errors or disputes that may arise in the future. The above four items are related to the consolidation of landowners' property rights and should be given special attention. This notice is hereby issued."

Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway Resumes Two Morning Express Trains

The Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Bureau's Transportation Department temporarily suspended the 4th express train from Shanghai to Hangzhou at 9:00 AM daily and the 1st express train from Hangzhou to Shanghai at 7:00 AM last month due to a shortage of vehicles. Minutes of the Nanshi Wharf Evaluation Committee

On the afternoon of the 24th of this month at 2:00 PM, the Port Authority convened the Nanshi Wharf Evaluation Committee to discuss various matters related to the reorganization of the Nanshi coastline wharves, with the participation of the heads of the Land, Public Works, and Finance Bureaus, as well as representatives from shipping companies. The following resolutions were made: (1) Regarding the discussion of the financial inventory reported by the Dada Company, it was found that the first item was already included in the existing wharves and did not need to be valued separately. The second and fourth items had already been offset against the loan from the former Municipal Council. Now that the loan has been repaid, it is naturally unnecessary to repay the loan item. The third item cannot be considered as property. The tenth and eleventh items were added to the contract in August 1917, stating that all annual dredging and maintenance expenses prior to the rent increase had been paid by the Dada Company in the amount of over 20,000 taels of silver, and would not be repaid by the council. There would be no further rent increases in the future, and the Dada Company would be responsible for the maintenance of the wooden hulls. Therefore, it is naturally impossible to request repayment again. In addition, the 5th, 6th, 7th, 8th, 9th, 12th, and 13th items will be depreciated annually according to the original reported prices. Should this be decided by the public? (Resolution) The 1st, 2nd, 3rd, 4th, 10th, 11th, and 6th items cannot be recognized for valuation based on the above reasons. The 5th, 6th, 7th, 8th, 9th, 12th, and 13th items will be depreciated according to their age and valued for repayment. (2) Regarding the discussion of the property inventory reported by the Minxing Company, it was found that the 1st and 2nd categories reported by the company were for company preparation expenses and property, which cannot be compared with wharf assets and should not be valued for recovery. As for the third category, the rent cannot be refunded. The security deposit will be used to offset the rent due, and the remainder will be refunded if there is a surplus. The 1st and 2nd items in the fourth category will be appropriately reduced for repayment. The 3rd and 4th items will be depreciated and valued for repayment according to the reported prices. Should this be decided by the public? (Resolution) The 1st, 2nd, and 3rd categories, as well as the 1st and 2nd items in the fourth category, will be handled according to the above method. However, the 3rd and 4th items in the fourth category will be recovered at the original prices reported by the company after verifying the evidence. (3) Regarding the discussion of the valuation inventory of various companies reported by the specialist committee, it was found that the valuation of Dada's No. 7 wharf was 1,000 taels higher than the company's original reported price, and the depreciation was not calculated according to age, which was somewhat excessive. Should it be re-evaluated and discussed? Please decide by public vote. (Resolution) The original committee will re-verify the valuation and provide copies of the original price lists reported by Dada and Minxing for reference.

Pacific Shipping Industry in Decline

Since the drastic reduction in fares by Japanese ships, Shanghai has faced a situation of many ships and few goods, with an oversupply of tonnage. Recently, with the reduction in freight rates by liners from New York, many Shanghai exports to the United States are being directly loaded onto New York ships, which has led to a sharp decline in exports on Pacific ships. The Osaka Company in the city has decided to suspend all its commercial ships on the Pacific line from coming to China for one month, starting today, to avoid unexpected losses such as tonnage fees.

Ms. Smith Withdraws from the Board of Directors Candidacy

Following the Wishes of the American Government

The Wenhui Bao reports that Ms. Smith, the American Commercial Attaché and member of the Board of Directors candidate, has withdrawn from the election this morning (27th) after receiving a telegram from the U.S. State Department, stating that it would be inappropriate for Ms. Smith to hold public office and participate in the election. She told the reporter from this newspaper that she feared that foreign parties might misunderstand and view her participation as a competition representing the U.S. government, so she withdrew from the candidacy. Initially, the women's community in the city wanted to take this opportunity to nominate a candidate and earnestly persuaded her to run. She knew that there might be difficulties on the part of the U.S. government, but she had always supported the principle of establishing female candidates and noted that women were listed in the Municipal Council's electoral roll together with consular officials and other diplomats, so she readily agreed. Now, no objections have been raised among the Municipal Council personnel regarding the nomination of female candidates or her eligibility for election. Her withdrawal is purely due to following the wishes of her government and avoiding causing misunderstandings from the outside world. However, she still hopes that the women in the city will continue to pay close attention to municipal affairs, exercise all their rights, and express her gratitude to those who support the women's election and the expansion of the scope of nomination of candidates. The well-intentioned publicity from the newspapers is also deeply appreciated.

Furthermore, the Municipal Council also officially stated yesterday that the bureau's authority cannot directly inform or petition the governments of London or Washington. Even formal letters to the ministers must be conveyed through the consul. As for formal petitions to the British and American governments, they must be forwarded by the British and American ministers. The bureau can never directly reach the two governments.

Appeal of the Ningtai Fish Merchants

The Wuchen News Agency reports that the Ningtai fish merchants issued a summary yesterday regarding the increase in commissions by various firms, requesting assistance from all sectors. The text reads: "We, the ice-fresh fish merchants, often transport fresh fish from the seas near Shengshan and Daishan to Shanghai, Ningbo, and other places, distributing them to various fish firms for sale on our behalf. The Dunhe Guild and various fish firms in Shanghai deduct numerous commission items from the sale price of our fish, according to past practice. First, they deduct 99%, then they deduct 9.88% from the 99%, and from the 9.88%, they deduct 9.3%, called 'firm commission,' and then they deduct 0.1%, called 'stack labor.' What is even more unreasonable is that the expenses of the guild organized by the firms are not borne by the firms themselves but are instead taken from the fish merchants, deducting another 0.1% from the aforementioned firm commission and stack labor, called 'public fee.' Therefore, the fish merchants only receive 90.3 yuan for every 100 yuan of fish value. In 1926, the firms, citing increased cost of living and huge expenses, added another 1% commission, so that we only receive 89.753 yuan for every 100 yuan. Alas, we fish merchants are small-scale businesses, risking danger in the open seas and pirate attacks. Because we lack knowledge and unity, we are at the mercy of others, enduring the pain. However, the firms are still not satisfied. Starting this year, they have suddenly added another 1% commission, claiming that they have obtained approval from the Social Affairs Bureau. We fish merchants can no longer tolerate this and are forced to make a final struggle. We hereby state the reasons for our opposition, hoping that you benevolent gentlemen will show compassion and examine the situation. First, the firms have again cited increased cost of living as the reason for this commission increase. It is not known that the commission was already increased by 1% in 1926, and the collective income of the firms has increased by about 100,000 yuan per year compared to before 1926. Only three years have passed, and they suddenly increased the commission again. How can the fish merchants endure this? Moreover, the increased cost of living is not only felt by the firms. The fish merchants also feel the pain of increased cost of living. Not only is there no compensation, but we must also bear the increased burden. In terms of sentiment and reason, how can this be considered fair? This is the first reason why we cannot agree. Second, in recent years, due to the intrusion of Japanese frozen fish into the market, most fish merchants have suffered losses. This is a fact that can be proven, and the firms also know this very well. Now, assuming that each fresh fish boat does 40,000 yuan of business per year, the increased commission will suddenly increase the loss by 400 yuan. Except for the boats that suffer losses, the boats that are fortunate enough to make a profit only make 300 to 500 yuan per boat. In that case, do we fish merchants still have hope of not suffering losses? This is the second reason why we cannot agree. Third, the business of fresh fish boats begins in September of each year and ends in August of the following year. The borrowing of funds and the hiring of partners all begin in September. Whether the business continues or not is also decided at this time. If the firms had announced the commission increase before September of last year, then we fish merchants would still have the freedom to consider whether or not it is worthwhile to continue the business. Now, they did not announce it in advance but secretly reported to the government offices to seek profit, leaving the fish merchants unable to advance or retreat. There is no way to avoid being completely exploited. This is close to entrapment. This is the third reason why we cannot agree. Fourth, the expenses of various industry guilds are borne by the industries themselves. This is the case in Shanghai and in every industry. Now, Dunhe is taking the funds from the fish merchants, forcing them to bear unexpected obligations. Since the extraction of public fees, it has been more than ten years. At 10,000 yuan per year, the burden that we fish merchants bear for the Dunhe Guild is almost more than 150,000 yuan. It can be said that this guild is owned by the fish merchants. Our hard-earned money is taken at will, but the fish merchants have absolutely no right to enjoy any benefits from the guild. This 0.1% public fee is only used to provide the guild's extravagance, superstition, and the weekly banquets of the firm managers. The world says there are oppressed classes. It is likely referring to us fish merchants. This is the fourth reason why we cannot agree. In summary, it can be seen whether the firms' sudden increase in commission and extraction of public fees is reasonable. We fish merchants are the weak and can only sincerely appeal to all the gentlemen in all sectors, hoping that they will have mercy on our difficult and oppressed situation and grant us salvation. We present our words with tears, only expressing a hundredth of our feelings. We are at your urgent command."

Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau Attempts to Manufacture Bovine Pest Serum

Our country's rural farmers mostly rely on cattle power for cultivation, but there is often the problem of cattle plague, which is actually caused by bovine pest. According to investigations, in the vicinity of Shanghai alone, a bovine pest outbreak occurred in early December of last year, affecting various dairy farms in Pudong. Later, it was completely stopped in mid-January of this year, thanks to serum relief. In less than two months, the various dairy farms had lost as many as 300 cattle. There are currently no domestic manufacturing facilities for this serum, which specifically treats bovine pest, and most of it must be supplied by foreigners at a very high cost, resulting in the outflow of profits, which is a great pity. In fact, manufacturing this serum is not difficult. With sufficient equipment and a few months of operation, a large quantity of products can be produced, sufficient to provide relief from bovine pest. The Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau, recognizing this, believes that although this undertaking is not within the scope of inspection, the experts' focus on academic research has always been advocated by the bureau. This matter is related to agricultural economy, and if it can be actively researched, it will have a great impact. Therefore, it has specifically opened up five mu of land in Jiangwan to engage in research. Veterinarian Yi Wenzhi from the Livestock Product Inspection Office brought back multiple bottles of bovine pest resistant serum and antitoxin from the Philippines. Currently, Yi Wenzhi is collaborating with the bureau's veterinarian Luo Qingsheng and technician Shou Biao to conduct trials, which have had a good response. It is expected that they will be able to manufacture and apply it in the near future.

A Tale of Wonder: Giant Rat Bites and Injures Three

The whole family startled awake in the middle of the night

Giant rat simultaneously bites and injures three

The rat escapes despite being injured by a stick

Nearby residents are uneasy

The Shanghai Times reports that in a residence at 36 Taiheng Li (transliteration), North Sichuan Road, on Tuesday night, a seven-year-old Chinese child suddenly cried out. His mother rushed to check and saw one large and one small rat jump off the bed. The child's lower lip was bleeding profusely, having been bitten by the rat in his sleep. The mother quickly got up to chase the rats, but while the small one escaped, the giant rat stood its ground and even lunged forward, biting the woman twice. The woman screamed, and the whole family gathered to help and capture the rat together. Although the rat was injured by a stick, it still managed to escape. Another person was also bitten on the ankle by the rat. The woman and her child have now been sent to the hospital. This matter was reported to the Chinese Health Bureau, which yesterday sent people with rat traps and other equipment to the residence to try to catch it, but they only caught two or three small rats. Now, the homes and shops in the surrounding area are all uneasy. Some say that they have recently seen a rat, huge and unnamed, which may be the culprit.

The Detective Team Cracked Another Kidnapping Case Yesterday

A ten-year-old hostage rescued

The kidnappers are still being strictly pursued

Since the City Public Security Bureau's detective team solved the Chen Tianxi kidnapping case, people in Shanghai have admired the team's swiftness in solving cases. Unexpectedly, yesterday morning, the team cracked another kidnapping case, rescuing the hostage on the spot. The details are recorded below:

Sudden secret report: Around two o'clock yesterday morning, Captain Qiao suddenly received a secret report from an informant, stating that Xu Jiarong, the young son of Xu Wanglun, a local resident of 55 Tanjiazhai, Zhabei, was kidnapped without a trace near the Sun Temple Jiaotong Road in Zhabei on January 3 of this year. It was learned that the hostage was currently hidden in Room 7 of a certain hotel in Taiyuan Fang, Xizilaihuo Street, Caishi Street, French Concession. Please send personnel to arrest them immediately, and so on. After receiving the report, Captain Qiao immediately gathered a large number of officers to make the arrest.

Hostage rescued: After receiving the report, Captain Qiao immediately joined Deputy Captain Lu Ying and led squad leader Wang Shifu, Su Sheng, detectives Wang Yao, Lu Xingchun, Dou Yulin, etc., in several cars to first report to the French General Police Station. The police chief immediately ordered several detectives to go with them. When they arrived at the hotel, they saw the name Zhu Fulin listed for Room 7 on the guest list. They then went upstairs together and found Room 7 locked. The room attendant said that last night (the 26th) at around eight o'clock, two men and one woman came with a child. This morning (yesterday), the men and women all went out together, ordering the door to be locked, saying that the child was lying in the room. They have not returned since leaving.

Personnel dispatched to guard: After the room attendant finished speaking, Captain Qi immediately ordered the door to be opened. They saw the young hostage lying on the bed and immediately rescued him. They then opened another room nearby, selected officers to guard it, and waited until dawn, but no one came. They immediately took the hostage back to the team and questioned him in detail about everything that happened. Although the hostage was only ten years old, he was unusually lively and immediately explained everything one by one, including how he was kidnapped that day, how he was transferred and hidden, how he missed his parents, and how he was abused by the kidnappers, until he escaped danger. Captain Qiao then ordered officers to notify the hostage's family and submitted a written report to the director.

Nine bandits in total: According to the hostage Xu Jiarong, whose milk name is Genfa, is ten years old. His father's name is Yulun, is thirty-six years old. His brother's name is Jiazhen, is seventeen. The eldest sister is Lanying, is twenty-one. The second sister is Lanzhen, is nineteen. There is also a one- or two-year-old younger brother. On January 3, at around four o'clock in the afternoon, he was returning home from school, passing near Jiaotong Road, when two bandits, one wearing an overcoat and one wearing an oilskin coat, each holding a pistol, grabbed me (the hostage referring to himself) and dragged me onto a rickshaw parked by the road, using the coat to cover me. Before long, we arrived at a place where I spent the night. There were nine bandits in total, with five guns. The next day, they sent me to the Jiangwan countryside, where I lived for a total of forty-seven days. Then, I was moved to 822 Jinyang Li, Peikai'er Road, Yangshupu, where I lived for six days. It was not until the night before last that I was brought to the hotel, and this morning (yesterday) I was rescued.

Searching everywhere: After Captain Qiao finished asking, he again ordered detectives Fu Zhengcai, Wang Yao, Lu Xingchun, Dou Yulin, Gao Juchuan, Wu Xiufeng, Han Ruisheng, Wang Zijun, Wu Zuorong, etc., to take the hostage and search in Jiangwan and Yangshupu. However, the hostage was very young, and also just returned from the bandits' den, and was still frightened, so he could not identify things clearly. The detectives returned to the team to report. Captain Qiao ordered a thorough investigation to be carried out, and those involved to be brought to justice.

Loss of Cash and Foreign Money After Leaving the Store, False Report of Theft and Robbery

More than one thousand yuan disappeared without a trace

Feared reprimand and fabricated a report

Fortunately, his character was usually good

Lenient punishment with a fine

Chen Ading, a Ningbo native who worked at the Beijing Road Coal Industry Bank, had been serving in the bank for more than eleven years. He was quite honest and usually made no mistakes in his work, so he was trusted. The day before yesterday, the bank manager ordered him to take more than four thousand yuan in banknotes and pay them to various banks. Chen first went to Sumitomo Bank on Jiujiang Road and paid 853 yuan. Then, he went to the Taiwan Bank on the Bund and paid 2,100 yuan. He also went to the Bank of China and paid 300 yuan. There was still 1,112.5 yuan left, which he planned to deliver to HSBC. Unexpectedly, after leaving the Bank of China, Chen reached into his pocket and found that the remaining banknotes had all disappeared. He was shocked and did not know how they were lost. Fearing reprimand, he acted impulsively without even considering the consequences. He went to the General Police Station and said that the banknotes in his pocket were intercepted by four bandits on the way out of the Bank of China. Two bandits held pistols and forced him into the alley next to the Longmao Foreign Firm on Guangdong Road, forcibly searching him and taking all the money. He requested an investigation. The police chief suspected Chen's story, as he would have had to pass four police posts from the Bank of China to Guangdong Road. Why didn't he report to the police post? The police chief immediately sent detective Pang Ruiqing and detective Zhang Jinlong to investigate, but there was no evidence to support Chen's claim. They then questioned Chen strictly. Chen was indeed guilty and finally confessed that the banknotes were lost. He was afraid of being punished, so he fabricated a report in the hope of evading responsibility. The police chief arrested him and sent him to the Provisional Court yesterday morning, prosecuting him for false accusation under Article 182 of the Criminal Law. Judge Zhou interrogated him. According to Chen's confession, he was confused after the loss, which led to this action. The bank hired lawyer Jiang Baoli to appear in court and state that the defendant's character was usually good. This time, he was afraid of being reprimanded, so he made a false report and requested lenient punishment. Judge Zhou then sentenced him to a lenient fine of 160 yuan as a warning.

Personal Methods to Avoid Meningitis

Formulated by the Health Director of the工部局

工部局 Notice No. 3937 states the following: Notice regarding the issuance of personal methods to avoid meningitis infection, for the purpose of preventing meningitis. In view of the fact that meningitis is very prevalent in Shanghai and its vicinity, the Health Director has formulated personal methods to avoid the disease. A special notice is hereby issued for public knowledge. These methods should be implemented promptly so that the disease will not spread. Everyone should pay attention and comply. The details are listed below: (1) Do not get close to people who are coughing or have a cold. (2) Use soft paper to catch the phlegm produced when coughing or sneezing, and burn it immediately after use. (3) Do not go to crowded places where the air is stagnant, humid, and microbes breed. (4) Try to protect children and young people from the dangers of this infection, as they are most susceptible to the disease and must be carefully protected. (5) Regularly rinse your throat and nose with mouthwash or a mild antiseptic solution. The easiest way to do this is to add half a spoon of salt or one spoon of 可利所安 (Glycerine of thymoe) to a cup of hot water, mix well, and use it. (6) All utensils used to hold food should be washed frequently with boiling water. (7) Frequently visit places with plenty of sunlight and ventilation, and live in houses with good air quality. (8) Adopt hygienic methods to increase your body's safety, so as to avoid all diseases. (9) If you have a cold, flu, sore throat, or vomiting, you should immediately go to bed and seek medical treatment. A special notice is hereby issued, and everyone is expected to be aware of it. This notice is issued on February 27, 1930, by General Manager Edward.

The Case of the Tyrant from Nantong Continued Yesterday

Teachers Xu Yanggao, Zhou Yixiu, and Li Jiagu, etc., reported that Xu Shanji, Wu Xuan, and other local bullies and gentry in the Xiting District of Nantong had embezzled huge sums of money. The case was publicly heard by the Shanghai District Court but was not concluded. Xu Shanji and Wu Xuan were released on bail pending further trial. At ten o'clock yesterday morning, Judge Deng opened the court for further hearing. The plaintiff's lawyer, Ma Junshuo, along with the plaintiffs Zhou Yixiu, Xu Yanggao, Li Jiagu, and witnesses Xu Botong, Xu Shiping, Qin Yueqing, etc., arrived in court one after another. The defendants Xu Shanji and Wu Xuan were not summoned. Lawyer Chen was delayed but appeared in court as their representative, requesting an adjournment. Zhou Yixiu briefly described the main points of the lawsuit, and then Xu Yanggao, Li Jiagu, and others each submitted written statements detailing how the defendants had encroached on the Second Five Treasury Bonds, arbitrarily established city loans, and engaged in illegal activities. Xu Botong testified that because the account books transferred by the former Municipal Office did not match, he convened local people to hold a review meeting. The meeting concluded that the accounts of the Second Five Treasury Bonds did not match, and that the city loans were extorted from the villagers by the defendants under false pretenses. The receipts and expenditure accounts for the river embankment fee and the land survey fee, as well as the maps, were never handed over. Xu Shiping testified that his family was solicited for eighty yuan in Second Five Treasury Bonds, which the defendant arbitrarily changed to a city loan. He said that the Second Five Treasury Bonds were a national loan, so the receipt was simply referred to as a loan. They repeatedly asked him to return the Second Five Treasury Bonds, but he said he had not received them. As for the announcement in the newspaper to solicit them, it was just a statement to the outside world. In reality, they could not get them back. The receipts he gave me were repeatedly requested and reissued after the money was received, and so on. Lawyer Ma said that there were many victims, most of whom did not come because they had no receipts. The official said that even without summonses, the victims were allowed to come on their own. Lawyer Ma also requested that the court open earlier to expedite the conclusion of the case. The judge agreed and ordered that since the defendants were not present today, the hearing would be adjourned to another date for review and judgment. The court was then adjourned.

Fierce Battle Between Police and Pirates at Da'an Port Outside Wusong Estuary

More than thirty pirates killed in battle

Five bandits captured alive and one hostage rescued

Chen Xin, the captain of the 18th team of the 4th district of the Wusong Water Police, suddenly received a secret report at around six o'clock in the morning the day before yesterday, stating that there were more than two hundred pirates aboard five large pirate ships near Xiaoyang Port, which belonged to the Tong area outside the Wusong estuary. After receiving the report, Captain Chen immediately ordered the second squad leader of the team to lead the entire team's patrol boat to quickly encircle and suppress them. When the patrol boat chased to Xiaoyang Port, the pirates had already received the news and raised their sails to escape. The patrol boat then pursued them from behind. When they met the pirate ships on the sea surface about five miles from Da'an Port, they immediately attacked. The pirate ships also resisted stubbornly. The gunfire from both sides was extremely fierce, and the battle lasted for five hours. More than thirty pirates were shot down into the water, and the pirates began to lose ground and flee. The patrol boat took advantage of the victory to pursue them and captured five pirates on the spot, and rescued one hostage. The patrol boat then ran out of ammunition and stopped pursuing them, allowing the pirate ships to escape. Captain Chen reported the situation to Zhu Bingzheng, the district chief of the fourth district, yesterday for the record.

Tragic Deaths are Often Heard

Wuhu native Xi Youfu, forty-six years old, tragically committed suicide by slitting his own throat. He was the head steward at the home of a certain Russian at 167 Guba Road, French Concession. The relationship between the host and guest was very harmonious. Xi suffered from a nervous disorder that flared up from time to time, but it is unknown why he suddenly had suicidal thoughts. At around six o'clock yesterday morning, he took a long knife and a pair of scissors used for work from the small room next to the kitchen of his master's house, sat on the edge of his bed, and slit his own throat. At that time, Xi fainted and fell to the ground due to the pain of having his throat cut, and blood covered the floor. The master discovered him and entered the room to check, and was horrified. He immediately reported to the police station, which sent detectives to investigate. Xi had already died. The wound was more than an inch deep. The knife used for the suicide was found next to the body and taken back to the police station. The detective reported to the police chief and notified the Tongren Zhuanyuantang to send staff to carry the body to the mortuary. Detectives were also sent to verify and summon Xi Youfu's brother, Xi Yousheng, and Xi Tang's, Xi's wife (who lived on Qiujiang Road, Hongkou) to the case. The Criminal Division reported to Judge Zhu of the French Concession, who arrived at the scene to examine the body. After taking his seat in public, Judge Zhu was informed by the detective of the previous situation. After questioning the family members of the deceased, Judge Zhu ordered that it be verified that the deceased had indeed committed suicide by slitting his own throat before his death, and that the family members should prepare a coffin and collect the body themselves.

Died of illness after drowning: On the 23rd of this month, a young man threw himself into the Huangpu River in the French Concession to commit suicide. The police caught sight of him, called for help from Xiuzi, and managed to rescue him. They took him to the police station. The police chief questioned him, but he only provided his surname, Wang, and his name, Junsheng, and his age, twenty-eight years old. He firmly refused to reveal the reason for his suicide. After the police chief found out that Wang was ill, he ordered him to be sent to Renji Hospital for treatment, but it was ineffective. He died the day before yesterday. The hospital notified the police station, which sent detectives to carry the body to the Tongren Fuyuantang mortuary. No family members were found. Yesterday, the police station reported to Judge Zhu of the French Concession, who arrived at the scene to verify that the deceased had indeed drowned and died of illness before his death. It was ordered that a photograph be taken and that Tongren Fuyuantang prepare a coffin and collect the body, and place it in the altar to await identification by family members.

Jiangbei child Zhang Amao, fourteen years old, was run over and killed by a car. He lived in a bungalow in Gujia Garden, Zhabei, and was a dock worker. At twelve o'clock yesterday afternoon, he was walking through the intersection of North Suzhou Road and Sichuan Road when he was suddenly run over and fatally injured by a certain truck. He died instantly. The driver, seeing that he had caused an accident, quickly sped away without a trace. Subsequently, police officer No. 2442 from the Huisi Police Station arrived at the scene, transported the body to Tongren Hospital, and then to the mortuary to await examination.

Jiangbei native Zhan Zicheng, a rickshaw puller, died of a sudden illness on the road. He lived at 90 Wangjiazhai, Zhabei. At seven o'clock yesterday morning, he took his rickshaw out to solicit passengers near Gaolang Bridge on Huade Road. He suddenly fell ill and collapsed on the ground. When Chinese policeman No. 1037 checked on him, he could not speak. He was transported to Tongren Hospital in a rickshaw, but by the time he arrived at the hospital gate, he had already died. The body was then carried to the Feilun Road mortuary. This morning, the police station reported to the Provisional Court, which commissioned Judge Luo Renji to arrive at the scene to verify that he had died of illness. He ordered Zhan Ziping, the deceased's brother, to sign a guarantee and collect the coffin.

Kidnappers Arrested in Baxianfang

At around three o'clock yesterday morning, the Water Police Team sent personnel to the French General Police Station to report that there were many kidnappers hiding in the house at 16 Baxianfang, Huagenao Road, within the concession, requesting assistance in the arrest. The police chief immediately ordered several Chinese and Western detectives to go to the address together. They arrested three people in the front building of the house and immediately took them to the police station. According to Mr. Xiang, the second landlord of No. 16, on the 21st day of the twelfth month of the old calendar last year, a man wearing a felt hat and a bamboo skirt, about thirty years old, came to rent the front building, agreeing to a monthly rent of seventeen yuan, and paying a deposit of six yuan first. When asked what he did for a living, he replied that he worked in a rice shop and had four or five people in his family, including his wife, mother-in-law, and children. He moved in on the 26th. No one came to visit at first. Around the 10th of this month, four or five people wearing felt hats and bamboo skirts came upstairs and stayed for several hours before leaving.

Until about three o'clock this morning, a large number of detectives came, along with an informant, and arrested three people. There were still a few young women, old women, and young children upstairs. It was said that one of the people arrested was Liu Xiaomei, and the other one or two were unknown. The young woman, Wu, was originally married to Zhou Zirong in Lili, but was later sold by Zhou and escaped after being abused. She met Liu's rice boat in the harbor, and was brought to Shanghai by Liu. She rented the house. Usually, Liu forbade her from eavesdropping on his conversations with friends. The old woman was Wu's biological mother, Li, who came to Shanghai from Lili two days ago because Wu was pregnant and about to give birth.

Supplementary Record of the Large Amount of Opium Seized on the Xianghe Steamer

The Shanghai Times reported that before dawn on Tuesday, the General Police Station's Anti-Narcotics Team, along with customs officials and water police, seized a large amount of opium worth 80,000 yuan on the Xianghe steamer from the Yangtze River and arrested two people, who were transferred to the Chinese authorities for punishment. Previously, the police had long known that there was a very large opium trafficking organization in this city, whose activities not only extended to the Yangtze River area but also throughout the country. This time, they learned that a large amount of Yunnan and Sichuan opium was being transported by the Xianghe. After the ship arrived in Shanghai and docked near Zhaofeng Road on Monday afternoon, the Western police knew that a portion of it would be secretly transported into the concession. Therefore, they secretly monitored it at night and learned that the organization had hired hundreds of secret agents to watch the surroundings and pay attention to the detectives. Therefore, their actions were very secretive. They later learned that these people had hired several cars to smuggle a large amount of opium ashore. They hid near the pier and secretly waited. After a long time, they saw someone giving the signal to start transporting. The police immediately came out, but several workers were already carrying several bags down from the ship and were about to leave the pier gate. However, these people caught sight of the police and one of them closed the door and locked it. The workers also quickly carried the goods they were carrying back to the ship. After several twists and turns, the police managed to open the pier gate and rushed to the ship. However, since the ship was docked outside the concession, there were difficulties. Fortunately, with the help of the shipowner, they were able to board the ship. When they checked near a government cabin, they smelled opium. However, the door was locked and the key could not be found. The shipowner and the chief mate helped to open a window. One policeman reached in and found a small package of opium, and there were two people guarding it. These two people also did not have a key and seemed to be locked inside. They immediately notified the customs officials and the water police. When the water police arrived, they broke down the door and found eight bags of opium in the cabin. They then searched the coal bunker and found sixteen bags. They transported the opium to the customs warehouse and transferred the two people arrested to the Chinese authorities. When the ship passed through Wusong, anti-narcotics personnel boarded the ship and searched it once. It is said that several taels of opium were found.

The Fu'an Life Insurance Company's Deng Zhongze fraud case continued with arguments yesterday, and the counterclaim portion was investigated. The counter-defendants Deng Wenhai and others stated that although they were directors in the Hong Kong company, the Chinese Fu'an Company was indeed falsely established by the defendant. However, they did not ask about the policy. I have paid thousands of yuan in life insurance premiums, and I was actually cheated, and so on. Wu Hanzhou briefly stated that the defendant claimed to be clearing up the accounts and refused to pay the fees. Later, I learned that the company was actually a scam, and so on. Wu Shutang was in Xuzhou and did not attend. His lawyer, Fei Guoxi, replied that the plaintiff's insurance premiums were usually paid one or two years late, but they were still accepted as usual. There are overdue receipts submitted as evidence. Shi then paid the fees and also received them, actually wanting to rely on all the premiums. After clearing up the accounts, why do you still use the name of Chinese Fu'an to collect the premiums for valid effective insurance policies? Moreover, the newspaper advertised by the defendant, one announced the clearing up of accounts, and the other still claimed that business was as usual, in order to continue his fraudulent means. When Judge Chen interrogated him, he said that the newspaper was printed in error. Now he said that the staff made a mistake. The testimony was inconsistent before and after, which is tantamount to confessing that his newspaper announcement was evidence of a crime. However, there is no reason for the counterclaim's false accusation. Please declare the counterclaim not guilty and decide the original lawsuit according to law, and so on. Young Woman and Yangzhou Mei Lanfang

The two are in love and do not want to separate

The world is getting worse, what a sigh

Liu Xu's, a woman from Yancheng, living at 285 Xiangqing Li, Shanhai Pass Road, Xin Zha, is over sixty years old. Her husband has been dead for many years. Her son, Xiang Sheng, married Liao, who is twenty-three years old, beautiful, and has given birth to a son who is two years old. Liao has always been well-behaved, but unexpectedly, last winter, she went to the Gonghe Yangzhou Theatre on Daohuangzhen Road, Zhabei, to watch a play and met the actor Dai Lanfang from 扬州. Dai is a famous 花旦 and is known as the Yangzhou Mei Lanfang. Therefore, Liao fell in love at first sight and an affair began. However, Dai was quite poor and all his daily expenses were completely dependent on Liao. They built a love nest at the fourth house in Yongxiang Li on Datong Road and often made secret appointments. Liao made excuses to visit relatives in Zhabei, and her husband did not suspect anything. However, recently, Xu noticed that her actions were strange and found that the ornaments and valuable clothes in her box had all disappeared. So she secretly investigated. Yesterday, she hugged her son and went to her lover's place. Liao secretly followed behind. When she arrived at the destination, she immediately broke in and reasoned with her, saying that my family is not poor, your husband is also a decent businessman, and you have already given birth to a son. Why do you do such a shameless thing? Quickly return with me, repent and start over. However, Liao not only did not agree but also said that I love him (referring to Dai) and want to grow old with him. I want to divorce your son. Xu listened to her words and was very angry. She went out and called the police on duty and took her daughter-in-law and Dai to the Fourth District General Office. After Xu complained about the previous situation, she questioned Liao, who confessed that Dai was born beautiful and she was willing to live with him. Dai also confessed that he was twenty-six years old and that the affair with her was her own free will. The verdict was given as 간통, and they were sent to the Bureau for interrogation.

Restrictions on Building Material Sheds for Living

Provisional Measures Established

Since the Shanghai Municipal Government strictly prohibited the construction of thatched sheds, ordinary people have often built material sheds in name only for residential purposes. The Public Works Bureau, noting the increasing number of these material sheds scattered throughout the city, which not only detract from the appearance of the city but also easily lead to fires, believes that strict measures are necessary for rectification. However, in consideration of the hardships faced by the people before widespread construction of affordable housing in various districts, it has been decided to allow ordinary people to build sheds for residential purposes in the less developed areas of the South Shanghai District, Zhabei District, and Yinxiang District. In other areas, it is strictly prohibited, demonstrating a restriction. The provisional measures for restricting and dismantling material sheds have been submitted to and approved by the Municipal Government.

Popularity of Dr. Qu's Obstetrics Textbook

Obstetrics and Gynecology expert Dr. Qu Shaoheng, drawing on twenty years of research experience, authored the textbook "Lecture Notes on Obstetrics." Since its publication last year, it has become quite popular. Commentators have praised its content as substantial, based on practical experience rather than mere theory. It covers the anatomy and physiology of female reproductive organs, the sperm and egg of male and female reproduction, the condition of the fetus in the uterus, prenatal care during pregnancy, and various unusual fetuses. It concludes with obstetric surgery. The entire book is over five hundred pages, finely printed on high-quality wood-free paper. It is not only a valuable resource for medical students but also a book that every family woman should have on hand. With the start of the school year, sales have been brisk. The price is five yuan per copy. The general distributor is Qu's Husband and Wife Hospital, No. 98 West Chang'an Street, Beiping. Branch sales offices are Qu Cheng Law Firm, M17 Meibig Road, Shanghai, and the World Book Company, Fourth Road.

Inexpensive German Copier

Since the advent of the German (Multi Kopy) suitcase copier,

it has shone brightly in the copier world. With existing copiers, a single sheet of stencil paper can only print two or three hundred copies before becoming blurry. This machine can print 20,000 copies without leaking ink. Its efficiency is more than a hundred times higher. The clarity of the print and the non-greasy nature of the ink, along with its portability, make it superior to ordinary equipment. The original price was thirty yuan per unit, but now, by ordering more from the manufacturer, the cost has been reduced. At a time when gold prices are soaring, the price has been reduced to twenty-four yuan, making it a rare opportunity for buyers. The stencils, steel plates, and ink used in this machine can also be sold retail and used in other machines to improve their performance. The China agent is the Commercial Press.

Weather Report

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated that the weather would be cloudy and cold. There would be rain along the coast south of the Yangtze River estuary, and occasional rainfall in the Yangtze River basin. The wind along the coast would be from the northwest to the northeast, while there would be north winds in the Yangtze River basin. Shanghai Concession Court of Appeal

Free Talk

A Laughing Matter

— Hai Ke

Horse (mocking the car) — You are a dead thing. You can only move by eating oil. Without oil, you are dead. What is so rare about that?

Car — Your belly is filled with grass. And you can only carry one person on your back. I can carry three, four, five, or six people without them complaining. What is so rare about you?

Man — My love, you are unwilling to marry me. Then do you not love me?

Woman Worker — No. I still love you. I am one year older than you. I am like your older sister. From now on, we will be like siblings.

Man — Then, sister, quickly give me five dollars. I want to go buy a book.

Actor — Yesterday, I played the biggest role in that "Wu Song" play.

Friend of the Actor — What role?

Actor — It was the tiger on Jingyang Ridge. Did you see how big the tiger was?

Painter — Do you think my oil painting "Big Storm" is good?

Friend of the Painter — Extremely good. It is as vivid as the real thing.

Painter — The day before yesterday, a friend came to see me. As soon as he saw this painting, he borrowed my raincoat, rain boots, and rain hat completely.

Soon-to-be-engaged young man — I want to change the name on this engagement ring. Is that okay?

Jewelry Store Technician — The original name is engraved very deeply. It is not easy to change.

The wages must look better.

Young Man — Okay. But this time, do not engrave it too deeply. Perhaps it will have to be changed again.

Novel Prize Method in the Philippine Chinese Conference

— Yan Wenchou

During the opening of the Chinese conference, large companies always use a shopping voucher method. After the closing ceremony, a lottery is drawn to award prizes.

This is a plan to promote business, but winning prizes by luck is a gambling activity. This is strictly prohibited by the laws of this place. It is necessary to compete with intelligence and thought. It is also an interesting event in a lively occasion.

First, there were two English newspapers run by Filipinos in Manila. One was the Herald, and the other was the Tribune, which competed to promote sales. The Tribune partnered with an insurance company. Anyone who subscribed to the newspaper for three months of the year would receive an insurance policy from a certain company. During this year, if they were injured in the streets by a car or carriage, they could receive an insurance payment of one thousand yuan. The newspaper's sales increased greatly among the working class at the time. As this Chinese conference was about to open, the Herald joined forces with sixteen companies (the Chinese-Philippine New Min Daily News also joined) to invest forty thousand yuan. They set up the world's nine great figures as the target, namely Thomas Edison of the United States, Madame Curie of France, Benito Mussolini of Italy, Chiang Kai-shek of China, George of England, Miguel Primo de Rivera of Spain, Manuel L. Quezon of the Philippines, Nishi Mikado of Japan, and Paul von Hindenburg of Germany. Anyone who purchased a month's worth of newspapers or purchased one yuan's worth of goods from each company would receive a voucher. The names of these nine great figures are printed on the voucher. Participants must rank these nine figures in order of their own fair criticism (i.e., list the numbers 1, 2, and 3 next to the names of these nine people). From the opening of the Chinese conference at eight o'clock in the morning on the 16th, vouchers could be submitted to a specially designated ticket counter. (The ticket collector stamps the ticket with the date and time of receipt.) The participating companies hired three famous figures from the academic community in advance to jointly propose the order of these nine great figures. The order was sealed in nine iron cabinets. After the closing of the Chinese conference, the tickets were opened. Those whose proposed order was the same as that of the judges would receive the first prize, or be ranked as the second or third prize winners depending on the time of submission. (Gratitude)

The Story of a Madman Biting a Dog

— Fang Fei

A mad dog biting a person can lead to death. The world views it as a terrifying event. Recently, a relative from Xixing came and recounted a news story that happened there last year about a madman biting a dog. Recounting it is quite amusing. Previously, in that village, there was a Yang family that made a fortune by raising silkworms. The four brothers all had no children. Only the second brother had adopted a child early on. Everyone considered him to be the only heir. The child was also very intelligent. He had studied at a school in Anhui. His studies were remarkable. Two years ago, he suddenly fell into the water and drowned while riding a bicycle. His father was deeply saddened by this. He was depressed all day. When he saw people, he cried and claimed that the Yang family had no descendants. Some people advised him to adopt another child and cultivate him. How could he know that the child would not be as good as the previous one? Yang said that heaven would not grant the Yang family an heir. Even if there were a hundred adopted children, they could not be relied upon. Those who heard this laughed at his pedantry. He accumulated resentment for a long time. Yang's nerves gradually showed abnormal signs. After a month, he became a madman. He cried, fought, and had no rationality all day. His family locked him in a back room and did not allow him to go out. After a few days, his mental state recovered somewhat. He begged to be allowed to go out for a walk. So, two strong men accompanied him to stroll around the village. On the way, a village dog barked madly at him. Yang suddenly jumped forward, grabbed the dog's neck, and hugged it tightly. He suddenly bit the dog's nose with his mouth. The dog howled loudly. The strong men rushed forward to rescue it. Yang then threw the dog away, crying loudly, saying, "It's like seeing my son come. So, I hugged him and kissed his cheek. How could he turn into a dog?" The villagers knew that his madness had recurred. They locked him in the original room again. He died soon after. The dog did not suffer serious injuries. It was treated with medicine and did not die. However, the area around its nose now has a very deep bite mark. It looks like it was born with it. When people see it, it is no longer as brave and good at barking as before. It seems to be afraid of something.

Newly Popular Parrot Disease

— Lü Bing

Recently, a strange disease has become newly popular in European countries. The disease is called parrot fever. Many newspapers in our country have also reported on it, but they are brief and lack detail. Now, I have found a Western magazine and translated some excerpts to clarify the truth.

Origin of the Disease The first patient to develop parrot fever was Thomas, a pharmacist from Stanforth Nye. When the disease was severe, a medical consultation was held, but the cause could not be determined for a long time. Later, he was asked if he kept a parrot, and it became clear that the disease was transmitted by the bird. Therefore, the name parrot fever became a sensation for a time.

Spread of the Disease Now, parrots have been imported from the South Sea Islands into Berlin, Germany. According to reports from various places, the transmission is very severe. Three people have died. It has been confirmed that they suffered from parrot fever. Therefore, the authorities must strictly inspect imported parrots. When necessary, they are strictly prohibited from landing. Households that keep parrots are also instructed not to come into contact with them.

Symptoms Parrots suffer from epidemic fever, which can be transmitted to humans. When it occurs, the lungs become inflamed and the body temperature increases abnormally. However, there is no need for people to protect each other from infection.

Previous Records Examining previous history, only three people in England had died from parrot fever by 1927. Also, in 1892, 500 parrots were imported into Paris. Among them, 300 died of illness one after another. As a result, 46 people were infected at the same time. As many as 16 people died.

Kite Anecdotes

— Zheng Yimei

Spring is just beginning. Tender willows are spreading green. It's time to fly kites. Kites are also known as paper eagles or kites. They have a long history. Chengzhai Miscellany says that Han Xin used a kite to measure the distance to Weiyang Palace when he was negotiating with Xi. Also, Unique Records says that when Hou Jing was besieging Taicheng, Jianwen made a paper kite and flew it into the air to send an urgent message to the outside. Thus, kites were not just a tool for games. Also, Xun Chu Lu says that Li Ye of the Five Dynasties made kites in the palace, using threads to take advantage of the wind for entertainment. Later, he put a bamboo flute on the kite's head to make the wind enter the bamboo and produce a sound like a zither, hence the name kite. According to this, only those with strings can be called kites. Not ordinary paper kites that are so called.

The form of paper kites. The kite makers often compete to innovate. Some are centipedes, others are butterflies with two wings. Others, such as the soaring peng, the swimming kun, and the beautiful form of the goddess Chang'e, are all vividly displayed in the clouds. It is a spectacle. Japanese people have imitated it as a pair of swallows. The production is even more ingenious. When released, they fly up and down, no less than a pair of swallows welcoming spring.

Flying kites should be done in the suburbs. Otherwise, the power lines are like spider webs, which are easy to disrupt. And violate the police regulations. Those who do this game should know this. Some fly kites at night with lights hanging from the ends of the lines. Bright in the sky, competing with the stars and moon. Added to the strings, the high wind blowing, the charm is cold. Especially the enjoyment of sight and hearing.

People in Gangzhong, on the Double Ninth Festival, often compete to fly kites on Bird Rock Mountain, Yu Mountain, and Ping Mountain. This adds a rhyme to the event of climbing high and inserting dogwood.

Wei Chun Garden was once a famous scenic spot in Shanghai. One spring day, the garden owner launched a kite festival. Chinese and Western people competed to fly. As Yang Yu said, "The neck is tied with a slender ribbon, and the feet follow a long rope," it was a great event for a time. Wu Youru once drew it and put it in the Painting Treasure.

I once had a mis-recorded article about kites, which said that a woman from Zhao Prefecture liked to fly kites. One day, it fell into a garden. The daughter of the garden owner, a young woman who loved beautiful things, picked up the kite and knew it belonged to a woman from Zhao Prefecture. She wrote a poem on it and sent it back to her. The woman also wrote a poem in reply and had a servant give it to the young man. The young man was overjoyed. However, the woman had already been promised to someone else. Later, rumors spread. The woman's parents heard about it and blamed her, so she hanged herself. There was nothing else. It was just a mistake of writing. Those who heard about it lamented it. At that time, Zhuang Liumen was talented but frivolous. He had been involved in a lawsuit with the woman's father, so he resented him. He composed a Legend of the Kite Mistake, which was full of slander.

Interesting History of Yan Jupeng's Record Cutting

— Mei Hua Guan Zhu

The advantages of Bei Kai records have been widely reported in various newspapers. The following story is about a small anecdote when the famous actor Yan Jupeng cut a record of "Visiting Mother in the Palace."

"Yang YanHui" in the Sitting in the Palace, a slow-tempo Xipi melody, was previously available in records by Lao Tan. However, due to time constraints, it only sang up to "Arriving in Northern Territory." The six sentences from "I want to go to the camp to see my mother" to "Mothers and sons will meet and reunite in dreams" were omitted. Those who bought the record regretted not being able to see the whole picture. When Bei Kai was recording, he spent a long time researching this play. Everyone agreed that only Yan Jupeng could inherit Lao Tan's mantle. Therefore, it was decided to invite Jupeng to record this play to make up for Lao Tan's shortcomings. Unexpectedly, Jupeng refused to try it easily, because there was jade in front of him. When asked why, he said, "How dare I wield a pen in front of Confucius?" Moreover, there are many knowledgeable people who know this play. The slightest flaw can be criticized. If I brazenly record it, those who don't know the story will laugh at me for being bold and reckless and accuse me of being a criminal of Tan." After saying this, he bowed deeply and declined repeatedly. Because he was determined, I did not force him. The next day, when we met, Jupeng seemed to have changed his mind. However, I had to declare in the newspaper that it was a passive act. I said, "What's so difficult about that? I will obey your orders in the future." Only then did the complete Sitting in the Palace finally succeed. Those who know the process often joked about Yan Jupeng being raped by the owner of the Plum Blossom Hall. (It is said that this record has been released and the results are excellent. Public opinion is also very good. Everyone said that Jupeng's tone is very much like Lao Tan's. This record will definitely win good reputation.)

Common Sense Tidbits

— Tang Bi Hua

If you knock over a kerosene lamp, do not use cold water to pour it on. Not only will it be ineffective, but it will also increase the power of the water. It is best to cover it with a cotton blanket. It will be extinguished immediately. Although a cotton blanket will be damaged, the disaster will be avoided.

When traveling, do not exchange names with strangers. Exchange business cards. Especially on ships, trains, and hotels. Be very careful. Because you are afraid of meeting bad people. They will take your name and business card to swindle and deceive. Be careful.

Other things can be introduced. But only doctors cannot. If the doctor cures the disease, he will be credited. If the doctor makes the disease worse, the person who introduced the doctor will be blamed.

When giving gifts to relatives and friends, you must choose gifts that suit their tastes and are practical. Otherwise, you will waste money. As the saying goes, "Give a sword to a hero, and give rouge to a beautiful woman." That's what it means.

Heart's Warmth (137)

— Bao Tianxiao

Chapter Nine: Famous Scholars Make Merry Playing Hide-and-Seek, A Charming Woman Indulges in Protecting Them

Ever since this chapter, after Zuo Shichen treated guests at the Mingjing Club, whenever there were social engagements, whether it was enjoying floral wine or dining at restaurants, whenever friends suggested outings, Zuo Shichen would always call for Ruiyun's attendance. He had always been indifferent to such gatherings, but now, seeing that others weren't proposing them, he couldn't help but initiate them himself. When it came to dining out, he initially hoped others would suggest calling for a singing girl. As soon as someone mentioned it, he would eagerly say, "Let me write the invitation!" If no one responded, he would suggest, "Why not call a few singing girls to liven things up?" He often said this. When people got excited, he would then write Rui's singing girl's name. If he was invited to a floral wine party, he wasn't very good at playing cards. Watching others play, he'd say, "Let's call a singing girl to relieve the boredom." Without realizing it, he'd reach into the fruit plate, take a chit, write Ruiyun's name, and have the room attendant send it out. After Ruiyun arrived, he used to feel like there was nothing to talk about, but now it seemed like there were many things to say out of nowhere. In reality, they were all irrelevant. For example, he might say, "Today, I saw a madwoman on the street." Zuo Shichen would then ask, "Is she a man or a woman?" She'd say, "It's a woman. People say she's a love-struck madwoman, very young, only in her twenties. Some say she's sick with lovesickness." Then they'd ask, "Why is she called a love-struck madwoman?" And so, the questions and the conversation would begin. Or, she might say, "Last night, our neighbor in business died—a helper. They say it was acute dysentery. He was dead in less than twelve hours." Then she would ask why he died so quickly and whether there were ghosts after death. Zuo Shichen would laugh and say, "I haven't died before, how would I know?" She'd say, "You've read books. Surely the books have something to say about it." A moment later, she would say, "My great aunt says she's seen ghosts. Ghosts exist!" Such conversations, though irrelevant, pleased Zuo Shichen because of her naive and earnest demeanor, and the way she gestured while speaking. He deliberately teased her into talking. However, others saw them whispering sweet nothings, heads close together, not knowing what they were saying. In reality, they were talking about other people's affairs. A fifteen-year-old girl didn't really know much about love. She longed to play, but her profession and her life didn't allow her any leisure time. Since she had hung up her nameplate and started as a singing girl, every day as soon as the electric lights came on, she would be dressed up, sitting in a rented car, running from one singing hall to another, from one restaurant to another, until after midnight, when her day's work was finally done. Because there were many singing engagements, there were often thirty or forty a day. At night, she would be extremely tired. As soon as her head hit the pillow, she would fall asleep.

And so it would be again the next night.
