Brief Record of February Yarn Delivery

The February yarn auction occurred at the beginning of the month, coinciding with the Lunar New Year, when gold prices surged, greatly stimulating public sentiment. As a result, retail investors rushed to short sell, and a major yarn factory firm persisted in not selling, resulting in an extremely firm situation, reaching a maximum of 166 taels and 6 qian. With the start of trading after the New Year, American cotton prices plummeted by more than 100 pound coins, and factory inventories increased daily, resulting in a sharp decline. Afterwards, around the 20th, overseas cotton yarn consistently continued to fall. The situation in the North was unsettled, and business on the Yangtze River stalled. Furthermore, due to poor harvests last year, many cloth factories in inland areas stopped production, and sales were completely cut off. The market situation increasingly trended downward. Although a certain yarn factory strongly tightened the market, it was to no avail. The minimum price reached 154 taels and 7 qian. The resulting delivery price was 156 taels, with a total value of 1,271,400 taels. 750 bales were self-delivered, and 7,400 bales were actually delivered, totaling 8,150 bales, including 2,400 bales of 20-count Five Fortunes, 2,300 bales of Shepherd, 850 bales of 16-count Globe, 300 bales of 10-count Three Sheep, 200 bales of Sailboat, 200 bales of Hongfu, 50 bales of Red Lotus Bee, 250 bales of Double Happiness, and 50 bales of Globe. The Process of February Han Cotton Delivery

Delivery Price: 35 Taels...Amount Reached 3,200 Dan

In the previous two months, the February Han cotton price increased due to skyrocketing gold prices and a lack of sources in Han. The market sentiment was extremely firm, reaching a maximum of 36 taels and 23 qian. 糧食米市銷活續堅

The rice market sales continued to be strong.

Yesterday, boats arriving at Zhabei were received, and market sales remained active. Changzhou, Wuxi, and Northern Japonica rice from Jiangsu were purchased and sold by merchants, with high-quality goods stabilizing, mid-grade rice continuing to be firm, and prices fluctuating by only half a cent per unit. However, the selling prices of retail sellers varied, due to different levels of interest from buyers. The movement of ordinary early rice was slightly brisk, with continuous arrivals, making it difficult for prices to rise; they barely maintained their original levels. The supply of high-quality Yangxian rice was not strong, demand was very high, and prices were slightly tight. Mid- to lower-grade rice was affected by large-scale price manipulations, leading to sluggish sales and flat prices. Loose transactions of Duzi Xian and Ke Bu Xian rice were active, and after prices softened, buyer sentiment improved, leading to a price increase of half a cent. Direct sales of Baiyuan rice were not as smooth as those in Southern Shanghai, leading to sluggish prices. Additionally, with thick inventories remaining, there was no possibility of a turnaround for the time being.

Around twenty boats carrying rice arrived in Southern Shanghai in the morning. Changzhou, Suzhou, Wuxi, and other Japonica rice varieties were purchased by customers from villages, Chongming, and Nantong, leading to smooth sales and a price increase of half a cent. However, transactions of this type of rice were small. Demand for early rice from the Southern gangs of Qingpu, Jinze, and Lianfeng was sluggish, and with ample supply and sufficient inventory, prices were flat and weak. The price of extra-high-quality rice had already fallen below 16 yuan. There was continued buying interest for Yangxian and Duzi Xian rice from other regions, and market momentum was lively. Due to poor conditions in Saigon, overall prices only increased slightly by one Chinese foot. The price of top-grade Xian rice was around 16.5 yuan. Transactions were changing; arrivals and sales were both competitive. Buyers still selected high-quality rice for purchase, and market conditions were firm.

麵粉又被金價提高

Flour Prices Further Increased by Gold Prices

Yesterday, after the opening of the flour market in the morning and afternoon, prices for all months suddenly saw a rapid increase, as the price of foreign wheat had already risen by a significant amount, and the high price of gold had reappeared. With the market value of 500 taels from beyond the customs and exchange rates necessarily shrinking, this phenomenon would inevitably create hidden obstacles when approaching foreign flour and wheat. Although it was impossible to predict how the situation would develop, those who were bullish were excited, leading to brisk buying in both the morning and afternoon markets. Temporary speculation led to aggressive buying. Apart from the current month, where the increase was slight due to the imminent end of the month, future months saw significant gains, partly due to a rebound after a sharp fall, and partly due to overseas price quotations. However, an overpricing in the market could easily lead to a severe decline, and those who were bullish should consider carefully. As a result, the current month increased by 1.75 cents, March increased by 2.75 cents, April increased by 3 cents, May increased by 2.75 cents, June increased by 0.5 cents, and July increased by 0.75 cents.

期麥疲後之大反動

A Major Rebound After Weakness in Wheat Futures

Yesterday, after the opening of the wheat futures market in the morning and afternoon, the market for all months saw a fierce rebound. With the rise in foreign wheat prices and the flour market also rising, the near-term months saw a great shock in confidence and very eager buying. This state was due to the previous days' overdone decline, leading to a very strong rebound upon any opportunity. As a result, March increased by 6 cents compared to the previous day, and July increased by a substantial 7 cents. Although sentiment was good for the new wheat in June and July, the increase was still flat, with June increasing by only 2 cents and July by 1 cent. The current wheat market price was still stable, as the standard, although showing a rebound, was only around 5.05 taels. Therefore, high-quality goods of all grades were similar to the standard, while mid-grade goods entered the 5.1 tael range. Prices opened at 5.06 taels for Suqian wheat, 5.05 taels for Yaowan wheat, 5.04 taels for Qingjiangpu wheat, 5.01 taels for Mingguang wheat, and 4.99 taels for Yangzhou wheat, with a total of over 2,000 packages.

糖市日車糖趨勢步升

Fine ground white sugar was priced at 7.15 to 7.75 taels, and No. 20 medium ground white sugar was priced at 6.85 taels, with few transactions, and the market appeared stable. Market conditions were all lively.

Yesterday, First Grade Tribute Satin and 6-pound Guo Ju Hongbiao, and other eastern goods all rose by 0.025 to 0.025 taels. However, 100+ shipments were sent by merchants from Hubei, mostly Fushou bleached cloth, priced at 8.4 taels. Merchants from Jiangxi and Changsha were also relatively active, while others were uninspired. Transactions in the local market were mostly for patterned goods, while the sale of common goods was very quiet. Newly arrived three-color Zigung wool was selling quite briskly, with Ronghua Fugui priced at 0.23 taels, Yuhuayuan at 0.225 taels, and blue-striped satin also seeing additional purchases. Ersunfu Zijinshan new stripes were all priced at 0.17 taels, Hanshansi Zijinshan at 0.1675 taels, and Kewei Meiren at 0.165 taels. Western plain silk saw a slight increase yesterday, as arrivals this year were quite limited, and those holding goods had high hopes. Yiji Shuanghudie and Luoshili Shimeitu were priced at 0.485 taels per French foot.

社會消息稿例

Submission Guidelines for Social News

(1) Text should be about domestic and foreign science, industry, commerce, rural areas.

(2) Health, aviation, exploration, customs, or urban life and other news is limited.

(3) Pictures are limited to various lyrical books about social life. Photos are qualified for seasonal, landscape, animal and plant, character, and news photography. Seasonal landscape photography, if there are women, is especially welcome.

(4) The number of words in each text should not exceed two thousand.

(5) Do not write on both sides of the paper.

(6) The manuscript should not be written horizontally, the words should not be scribbled, and the Western text should be saved as much as possible. If the original text must be quoted, it must be attached under the translation.

(7) Do not draw pictures with blue ink, and do not use colored paper. White paper and black drawing must be used.

(8) Please indicate that the submission is for the Social News Department.

(9) All submissions will not be returned, whether published or not. If you need to return it, please state in advance and attach sufficient postage.

(10) Remuneration is divided into three types: 3 yuan, 2 yuan, and 1 yuan per thousand words. The same example applies to pictures and photos per frame. If there are special manuscripts, the remuneration will be calculated separately.

Social News

Recent Developments in Sports and Exercise in Europe and America

Women Exercising Nude in Sunlight

According to a certain gentleman returning from Europe and America, sports and exercise in Europe and America have recently become more developed. Germany has a sports league, dividing the country into 17 districts, and each district is divided into 20 to 30 small regions, with the smallest sports organization in the small region as the smallest unit. Its organization is prevalent throughout the country, with most citizens joining, with 5 million members and 2 million associate members, one-fifth of whom are women. A sports commemorative event is held every five years. In recent years, when the meeting was held in Keroth, 500,000 ordinary athletes gathered. The Prussian Sports School in Spander advocates "returning to nature," and women exercise nude in sunlight without being ashamed. The foot exercises extend forward, backward, and upward, like dancing, so that the limbs are stretched and the pelvic bones are strong and easy to produce. The corrective exercises initiated by the Dane P. H. Ling are also popular in Germany. In particular, according to the various machines of the American YMCA, exercising can correct lighter deformities of the human body, such as spinal curvature and left shoulder upward. In schools, etc., school doctors and physical education teachers work together to do this. As for the UK, it is a country of sports. If four or five people gather, they will engage in sports, such as golf, polo, and hunting. Women are also very active. In Italy under Mussolini, the slogan is first sports, second moral education, and third intellectual education. Mussolini himself serves as a role model to encourage them. In the United States, Mrs. Hoover serves as the female minister of the National General Sports Association and vigorously encourages sports.

Chinese Egg Imports to Japan Greatly Reduced

From 10 Million Yen to 1 Million Yen Annually

Reason: The Japanese Poultry Industry is Developed

Reason: Chinese Eggs are More Expensive

According to Japanese news, Japan's egg production has increased in recent years, and Chinese egg imports have been greatly reduced. Before 1928, the average annual import of Chinese eggs was worth more than 10 million yen. By 1928, it had been reduced to 6.9 million yen, and by 1929, it had been reduced to 3.9 million yen. It is predicted that the value of Chinese eggs imported this year will be less than 1 million yen. Half of the reason is the increase in Japanese egg production, and half is that Chinese eggs are more expensive than Japanese eggs. In recent years, Japan's poultry industry has developed, and egg prices have gradually fallen. All industries that use eggs as raw materials have also switched to using domestically produced Japanese eggs. Since the beginning of this year, few Chinese eggs have arrived in the Kansai market, and no Chinese eggs have been imported into Kanto.

Chinese Students Enrolling in Japanese Military Academies

Tokyo News: According to the announcement of the Japanese Ministry of the Army, 238 Chinese students applied for the Military Academy this year, and 90 were accepted, including Li Zhi, the wife's younger brother of Feng Yuxiang, Sun Jinghua, the wife's younger brother of Chen Tiaoyuan, Chen Zhuo, the younger brother of the naval commander Chen, and Chuan Pu, the younger brother of the Tianjin garrison commander Chuan Zuoyi. The enrollment period is stipulated to be from April 1 to the end of September. The academic period is from October 1 this year to July 1932.

A Sharp Increase in Mail During Japanese General Elections

Post Offices Hire 170,000 Temporary Workers

Tokyo News: During the recent Japanese general election, the amount of mail greatly increased. Post offices temporarily hired 170,000 people, and the Ministry of Communications increased expenditures by 1.8 million. As of the 19th, post offices across the country had received and sent 50 million election letters and postcards. A total of 500,000 people were busy working during the last few hours.

Polygamy Among Muslims in the Philippines

To be Abolished in Twenty Years

Manila News: The residents of Mindanao and Sulu Islands in the Philippines are mostly Muslims, who follow the Koran and still practice polygamy. Although American law prohibits it, it has not been effective. Recently, the Philippine Council proposed an amendment to the marriage law, which was approved by Governor Davis and passed by the Council. The content is to gradually abolish polygamy, and completely abolish it after 20 years. Generally, Christians advocate complete abolition immediately, but because Muslims in the Philippines and Moros object, there are fears of armed riots. Therefore, the authorities decided to adopt a gradual approach.

Overview of China's Annual Imports and Exports

According to the announcement of Mr. Kato, the deputy consul of Japan in Shanghai, the actual number of import and export trades in China last year was 129.8 million taels for imports and 112.7 million taels for exports, totaling 242.5 million taels. Compared with the previous year, the total increased by nearly 20%, and increased by 26% compared with the year before the previous year. The breakdown by region is listed below (unit: 1,000 customs taels):

Imports　　Exports

Shanghai　626,000　461,000

Hankou　35,000　16,000

Qingdao　54,000　24,000

Tianjin　53,000　78,500

Dalian　128,000　203,000

As shown in the table above, compared with the previous year, Shanghai, Qingdao, and Dalian increased in imports, while Hankou and Tianjin decreased. Shanghai and Dalian increased in exports, while Hankou, Qingdao, and Tianjin decreased. Hankou decreased greatly in both imports and exports. The increase in Shanghai was due to the revision of tariffs starting on February 1, and early imports were popular. The increase in Dalian was due to the relationship between China and Russia. The increase in Qingdao was due to the resolution of the Jiaoji Railway issue. The sharp decline in Hankou was due to the war and the interruption of traffic on the Pinghan Railway. The decrease in Tianjin was no more than the impact of the current situation.

According to a radiogram from the Byrd Antarctic Expedition, the expedition, which was trapped by ice, left Little America on the 20th on the "City of New York" and returned to the United States. Women's Life

New Year's Eve by Liu Qingqing

A Letter Sent from a Foreign Country

Dear Elder Sister Shijun,

"The fleeting years do not linger for youth." Truly, I now deeply feel the ruthlessness of time. Last year on New Year's Eve, you were all nestled gently in our loving mother's embrace. I was adrift at sea, and our younger sister was in Hunan Province at the Fourth Middle School. You wrote to tell me that on the thirtieth day of the twelfth lunar month, as the maid and sister-in-law filled the round table with New Year's dishes, and everyone gathered to eat the New Year's Eve dinner, Mother, missing her two daughters scattered far and wide, couldn't swallow the delicious food, because her throat was choked with tears. Sister, this very day this year, I am once again driven by life to a lonely foreign land. Our clever and adorable younger sister has been crowned queen of her earthen kingdom by disease and money. Today, I wonder if Mother's tears will be many times more than in previous years.

Overseas Chinese still preserve the ancient customs of the old year. On this thirtieth day, just like in China, they habitually eat New Year's Eve dinner, wear new clothes, respect the gods and ancestors, and set off firecrackers as New Year's celebrations. Sister, can you imagine how I feel when I hear these sounds?

Schools in China usually start their New Year holidays half a month in advance, but it's not the same here. Even though today is the thirtieth day of the twelfth lunar month, Huiqing's school hasn't started the holiday. It's because the stubborn principal wants to please those illiterate but wealthy school board members. Having classes on the thirtieth of the twelfth lunar month shows that he is an educator devoted to education. Huiqing went to class, and I went with her. I hid in the deep shade of the schoolyard reading books. She stubbornly stayed in the classroom, holding a teaching whip, touching chalk, raising her voice, and standing on the podium talking tirelessly. Her classes ended at six o'clock, and it was already three in the afternoon. We went back to our dormitory together, hunger driving us to seek food in that low-lying house. Alas, our tin pot, brass stove, porcelain bowls, bone chopsticks, etc., had all been stolen by the runaway maid. Our New Year's Eve dinner naturally became just a painting of a cake. We thought about buying some snacks outside for our New Year's Eve meal. But since we just arrived here, we don't speak the language well, and even saying a single sentence is difficult. Besides knowing the transliteration of "bread" as "lao di er," we don't understand the names of any other food. So, our New Year's Eve dinner will naturally be two loaves of bread.

Around three in the afternoon, some students' families sent some snacks, fruits, and ice soda. Our food for tomorrow, or rather, our food for the coming year, can be considered secured. Although we are very poor and lonely abroad, I always feel like I am happy, because this special kind of life in a foreign country still has some interest.

A noisy sound came from outside, mixed with a sharp and piercing sound. When I went out to take a look, it turned out that the local people were dancing to entertain the capitalists. Two girls, about sixteen years old, had skin like smoked yellow bacon. Their chests and legs were covered with dance costumes woven from coconut tree hair. They wore egg-sized copper earrings and held red veils in their hands. Their dancing was lively and natural. I thought, if these women were in a civilized country and given training, their art might be outstanding and graceful. This kind of dance is something I've seen for the first time in my life. Because today is New Year's, it's a happy day for the rich. For people like us, who haven't had a grain of rice in our stomachs today, feasting our eyes is enough to satisfy us.

Some children on the street, wearing new clothes, were standing outside their doors, playing with firecrackers in their hands. I couldn't help but think of my own childhood. Before New Year's even arrived, my brother had already returned from school. He would write couplets and always ask me to grind ink. At that time, my little hands had so much difficulty grinding a tray of thick ink. So, I made a deal with him: a tray of thick ink for a large string of Liuyang firecrackers. Later, my small wooden bookcase was filled with them. On the night of the thirtieth, Mother dressed me in fancy clothes, hung a snake-like New Year's lucky money made of red rope around my neck, and I also held many firecrackers and incense sticks in my hand, standing in front of the door playing like these children. At that time, I was very happy, so I really looked forward to New Year's. New Year's seems to be the endless hope of children; it is also the sad disappointment of the elderly.

Tonight in China, every family will close their doors and windows, and the whole family will gather around the stove to stay up late, quietly spending a happy New Year. The New Year's situation here is completely different from in China. Although every household's door is decorated with lanterns and colored streamers, some people are wearing silk and satin clothes, holding round fans, and sitting on the brightly lit verandas enjoying the cool air. Everywhere, you can only hear chaotic clamor, noisy drum and gong sounds, and crackling firecrackers. All these sounds mixed together in this hot weather and dry air make it even more unbearable. So, Huiqing and I escaped from this foul air to the park to look for a trace of wind. My eyes completely fell on the dull, standing treetops. The branches and leaves seemed to be sleeping, and the surrounding birds were all quietly silent.

We slowly strolled to the pond. Many men and women, whom my eyes were meeting for the first time, were also sitting here waiting for the wind god to descend. We sat on a long bench on the bridgehead, and the lights on the opposite bank of a large river were reflected in the water, with thousands of rays of golden light. It was truly beautiful.

This New Year's Eve, I found so many treasures of memories and also picked up so many unique tunes from this foreign land. All of this is a seed of memory planted in my heart. I am always afraid that the harvest will be somewhat painful. Younger sister Yueying, sent from a foreign country.

Marriage and Sorcery of the Maori People of New Zealand's Island

The Maori people on New Zealand Island, a British colony, are a very unique race. After decades of white people's management, they have not made much progress. They still practice the chieftain system and in many places stand in opposition to the white people.

Recently, C. R. Browne risked writing about the Maori people's sorcery during his confinement among the Maori people in "Maori Witchery." This book is a very interesting book full of barbaric descriptions. Regarding the situation where Moffat was captured and imprisoned by the Maori when the white people wanted to build a railway on the island: "I think their treatment of a prisoner is so kind that it has never been seen in a white people's prison. However, after a few days, some children peeped through the cracks and said to each other, 'Oh, these things are getting fat. Alas, it's time to kill them.' This made me anxiously think about my dangerous position. I decided to try my best to escape.

Undoubtedly, I am among those who are going to be killed. I am bound to be killed and eaten by these savage barbarians!"

But he did not escape; instead, he gained freedom and was released. Among these people was the author, Mr. Browne. After being released from prison, he spent a long time with them and married a Maori woman. The woman's name was Te Artu, a beautiful woman from the Maori aristocracy, a relative of Chief Ngatae. The wedding ceremony was very simple. After all the people in the village held a dance, they performed a solemn oath-taking ceremony for the bride and groom.

"There is a very important question to ask you, Para," Chief said. "That is, do you promise to always be faithful to Te Artu? While she lives, you will never have relations with any other woman?"

"I am very happy to allow that, oh, Ngatae," I replied.

Then the chief shouted loudly and clearly, "Oh, people of Tuhva, relatives of my niece, do you want this white Para to be Te Artu's husband?"

They all shouted in unison, "Yes!" Only Tojjhiora, who resembled a high priest among white people, did not express his approval.

In fact, he had a very high position in the Maori tribe. After the chief lectured me and the bride and told us that our marriage was appropriate, the high priest stood up and cursed me, saying that our marriage would not last long and that we would soon die.

Browne said that he never returned to the one he loved. Their home was destroyed, and his bride was killed under the supervision of the sorcery-performing high priest, who considered her unlucky, after her husband was away from home.
